### [India’s consumption numbers fit into our big picture of progress](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-consumption-numbers-fit-into-our-big-picture-of-progress-11709483131073.html)

The Household Consumption Expenditure Survey (HCES) for 2022-23 reveals promising trends in India's economic growth. Over the past decade, monthly per capita expenditure increased significantly, with a 40% rise in rural areas and 33.5% in urban areas. Notably, the rural-urban divide has narrowed, dropping from an 83.9% gap in 2011-12 to 71.2% in 2022-23.

The survey also indicates a decline in economic inequality, with the bottom 5% of the population experiencing faster consumption growth (9.2% rural and 10% urban) than the top 5% (8% rural and 6.6% urban). This inclusive growth is further evidenced by rising MPCE/GNI ratios for lower-income groups.

The HCES attributes these positive developments to investments in infrastructure and empowerment programs, such as rural road expansion, women's collectives, and the Mahatma Gandhi National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme. The survey highlights the impact of government-provided free-of-cost items, underscoring the improvement in living standards beyond what consumption data suggests.

While the survey provides valuable insights, the authors note that future iterations could enhance coverage of government support and update consumer baskets and poverty lines in line with evolving aspirations. Overall, the HCES 2022-23 results support the government's approach of growth through infrastructure and inclusion through empowerment.

### [Revitalizing India's cotton saga: A blueprint for growth](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/first-person/revitalizing-indias-cotton-saga-a-blueprint-for-growth-11709371029223.html)

India, the world's second-largest cotton producer, faces dwindling cotton yields due to pest resistance and unpredictable weather patterns. The decline in yield has prompted farmers to switch to other crops, threatening India's cotton production and self-sufficiency.

Revitalizing Bt Cotton: The initial success of genetically modified Bt cotton, designed to resist bollworms, has led to over-reliance. This dependency has resulted in stagnant and declining yields. To address this, the development and deployment of new Bt cotton varieties and more effective pesticides and insecticides is crucial.

Precision Agriculture: Cotton is water-intensive. Adopting precision agriculture techniques like drip irrigation can reduce water and fertilizer consumption while increasing yields. Targeted delivery of nutrients through precision agriculture is also seen as critical for yield improvement.

Embracing Digitization: Digitization holds immense potential for transforming cotton farming. Drones can scan large areas for pest infestations, while satellites can monitor weather patterns and provide farmers with essential information. AI and IoT can assist farmers in making informed decisions on crop protection and nutritional interventions.

Tried and Tested Practices: Pairing new technologies with tried and tested agricultural practices is essential. Weed infestation significantly affects yields. Implementing early-stage weed management, crop rotation, compost application, and green manuring can help minimize weed impact and support soil health.

Collective Action: Revitalizing India's cotton sector requires collective action, collaboration, and a shared commitment among stakeholders, including agricultural scientists, regulatory bodies, and the agrochemical industry. Technological advancements and sustainable farming practices are key to restoring India's position as a leading cotton producer and ensuring self-sufficiency.

Sat, 02 Mar 2024 12:22:39 +0530
### [How Isro’s ‘naughty boy’ cryogenic engine became a ‘smart boy’](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/how-isro-s-naughty-boy-cryogenic-engine-became-a-smart-boy-11709355686013.html)

On March 30th, NASA and ISRO will launch the NISAR satellite to gather data on Earth's ecosystems, ice masses, and sea level rise. The launch will utilize ISRO's GSLVF14 rocket, now nicknamed the "smart boy" after its successful launch.

The GSLVF14's cryogenic engine was developed by ISRO after US sanctions prevented technology transfers. Despite initial failures, the engine has been perfected and will significantly enhance India's aerospace industry. Its higher thrust-to-weight ratio allows for heavier payloads, paving the way for future Moon, Mars, and space station missions.

Cryogenic engines also play a role in the global satellite market and in military applications. India's mastery of this technology positions it as a major player in the aerospace sector and provides strategic comfort in a tense geopolitical climate.

### [How to master the art of delegation](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/how-to-master-the-art-of-delegation-11709279744423.html)

Delegation is crucial for effective management but can be challenging. Some managers avoid it due to mistrust, control issues, or previous startup experience. Others delegate for negative reasons like making difficult decisions or avoiding blame. Studies show that people tend to delegate when tasks are complex, affect others, or involve risk. To delegate effectively, establish a decision-making framework to clarify responsibilities. Distinguish between irreversible "type-1" and reversible "type-2" decisions. Allow subordinates some autonomy and avoid micromanaging, while maintaining involvement and decision-making authority when necessary. Like building abdominal muscles, delegation requires judgment, balance, and discipline.

### [There’s also a positive side of GenAI that can strengthen democracy](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/theres-also-a-positive-side-of-genai-that-can-strengthen-democracy-11709219220730.html)

As AI's ethical concerns emerge, 2024 promises a test of its impact on democracy. While deepfakes threaten to manipulate elections through misinformation, they have also been used strategically, as in Pakistan, where GenAI helped a jailed ex-prime minister's party win.

AI offers potential benefits for elections:

* **Transparency and Fraud Detection:** AI can monitor election data for irregularities and identify patterns of fraudulent activity.
* **Security Enhancement:** AI algorithms can improve the security of electronic voting systems and detect potential cyber threats.
* **Personalized Voter Education:** Generative AI can create customized content on candidates and issues, empowering marginalized groups.
* **Accessibility for Disabled Voters:** AI-powered systems can assist voters with disabilities in casting their votes.
* **Social Media Analysis:** AI can analyze social media information to gauge public opinion and ensure diverse representation in political discussions.
* **Logistics Optimization:** AI can streamline voter registration and verification, reducing queues and saving costs.

While acknowledging the risks of deepfakes, the article highlights that AI can also enhance democracy by improving transparency, inclusivity, and efficiency.

### [India-EU trade mustn’t stumble on digital sovereignty](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indiaeu-trade-mustn-t-stumble-on-digital-sovereignty-11709219303430.html)

The EU's recent digital policy initiatives, including the Digital Services Act (DSA) and a white-paper on infrastructure, aim to increase digital sovereignty and regulatory control. However, these initiatives conflict with the EU's goal of accelerating digital trade, particularly with India, as they impose complex compliance obligations for Indian internet companies.

The EU's strict regulatory approach, guided by legal sovereignty, limits exceptions for FTAs and creates uncertainty for trade. Additionally, the EU's ex-ante regulation approach for digital markets, echoed in India's plans, complicates negotiations due to different forecasts of future risks.

Despite these challenges, both the EU and India acknowledge the potential of digital technology for economic growth. India can leverage its software and services capabilities to support Europe's digital transformation, while Europe must find ways to reduce its reliance on foreign digital infrastructure.

To foster collaboration, India should focus on innovation-friendly regulations and advocate for liberalization of EU digital markets. The EU, in turn, should collaborate with India to decrease its dependence on foreign technology. Both parties need flexible policy strategies to remain relevant in the evolving digital landscape.

### [State-level rumbles in the Indian federation: Can the 16th FC help?](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/statelevel-rumbles-in-the-indian-federation-can-the-16th-fc-help-11709207501212.html)

Amidst farmer unrest, there is concern about unfair fiscal treatment of states by the Union government. States receive a percentage of gross taxes collected by the Centre, as prescribed by Finance Commissions every five years. However, states allege that Central cesses and surcharges, which are excluded from the shareable revenue base, are used to reduce their statutory payments.

In 2022-23, states received 31.1% of the reported gross tax revenue, significantly below the adjusted target of 40.8%. This shortfall is attributed to the exclusion of cesses. Including statutory grants and non-statutory flows, states received a total of 57.8% of gross Central tax revenue (excluding GST cess).

The dissatisfaction arises from the statutory tax share being 8.3% below the target. The upcoming 16th Finance Commission is encouraged to incentivize the Centre to merge cesses into the basic tax structure in exchange for a lower aggregate share for states. The lesson is that the states' effective tax share can languish near its pre-ramp-up level if cesses and surcharges are excluded from the shareable revenue base.

While some things, like student enrollment, can be easily counted, others, such as the number of trees, leaves, or bubbles in a cup of coffee, are much more challenging. Despite the apparent finiteness of these quantities, the act of counting them can be infinite due to the constant addition of new elements. ### [Fakeness and flakiness are not hard to spot in the social sector](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/fakeness-and-flakiness-are-not-hard-to-spot-in-the-social-sector-11709131249193.html)

The author criticizes the use of the term "partner" for NGOs receiving funding, arguing that it misrepresents the relationship as equal. They observe that donors often profess virtues like treating grantees as equals but may act differently, a form of "fakeness" in the social sector.

The author introduces a "fake-flake" matrix to categorize organizations:

* **Fake-fake:** Intellectual and relational fakeness, without operational or ethical rigor
* **Authentic-flake:** Intellectual and relational authenticity, but operational and ethical flakiness
* **Fake-rigorous:** Intellectual and operational rigor, but relational and ethical fakeness
* **Authentic-rigorous:** Intellectual, operational, relational, and ethical authenticity and rigor

The author believes that "fake-flakes" are easily noticed, while "fake-rigorous" are subtle and insidious, but that "authentic-rigorous" organizations are effective and common. They acknowledge that some degree of fakeness and flakiness is inevitable but emphasize the importance of authenticity and rigor in the social sector.

### [Revaluation call: Don’t write off businesses challenged by sunrise rivalry](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/revaluation-call-don-t-write-off-businesses-challenged-by-sunrise-rivalry-11709123217427.html)

Despite the perception that certain sectors (newspapers, thermal power, combustion engines) are dying out, they remain prevalent in reality. Investors overly focus on the potential decline of these sectors, leading to undervalued stocks.

Using a "zero-terminal-value discounted cash flow analysis" can help assess these undervalued stocks, assuming the company will eventually cease operations. However, this approach ignores potential upside scenarios, such as demand revival.

Factors contributing to the resurgence of undervalued stocks include tempered excitement for new technologies, strategic shifts by incumbent companies, and increased cash returns to shareholders. As interest rates rise, the value of steady cash flows increases.

Unexpected demand revivals can lead to significant price increases for incumbents in these sectors. Investors should consider evaluating these "forgotten stars" for potential value, recognizing that market perceptions can be overblown.

### [The EU is planning clear emission-capture norms for its carbon market](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-eu-is-planning-clear-emission-capture-norms-for-its-carbon-market-11709122921660.html)

The European Union (EU) is establishing a Carbon Removal Certification Framework (CRCF) and Green Claims Directive to regulate the carbon market.

The CRCF defines "carbon removal" as capturing and storing CO2 from the atmosphere. The Green Claims Directive requires companies to obtain approval for green marketing claims, which must include certified carbon removal offsets.

Companies can only claim to offset emissions that cannot be reduced further. Carbon credits must be certified under the CRCF, which excludes fossil-fuel emissions and temporary removals like tree planting.

The regulations set standards for certifying carbon removal credits, creating trust and distinguishing them from existing poor-quality products. Companies can still purchase non-certified credits, but they cannot make environmental claims associated with them.

Despite potential limitations, the regulations aim to prevent greenwashing and establish clear standards for carbon removal and offsetting.

### [Indian households are investing more in stocks than it may seem](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indian-households-are-investing-more-in-stocks-than-it-may-seem-11709046613931.html)

Nilesh Shah's tweet suggests that Indian households invest little in stocks. However, this is an incomplete analysis.

From 2020 to 2023, 94% of household savings went to fixed-income investments like fixed deposits and life insurance, while only 6% went to mutual funds (MFs) and stocks.

However, some insurance premiums and EPFO contributions are invested in stocks indirectly, indicating that households invest more in stocks than the data suggests.

Despite this, the majority of household savings still go to low-risk fixed-income investments. Factors such as risk aversion, tax benefits of insurance, and effective MF advertising have contributed to this trend.

However, the share of household savings held in MFs has increased significantly in recent years, indicating a gradual shift towards equity investments.

Wed, 28 Feb 2024 03:30:52 +0530
### [India’s household consumption survey captures predictable changes](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-household-consumption-survey-captures-predictable-changes-11709046735551.html)

A fact sheet highlighting the Household Consumption Expenditure Survey (HCES) for 2022-23 was released. This survey covered approximately 100,000 urban and 150,000 rural households, indicating that the urban population comprises two-fifths of the total. The data demonstrates a transition in consumption patterns, moving from cereals to non-cereals, carbohydrates to proteins, home-cooked meals to packaged food, and food to non-food items. However, the consumption spending growth pace in urban India is higher than in rural areas, leading to a divergence in spending and partly explaining the north-south divide. The survey also reveals a slowdown in consumption spending across surveys conducted from 2004-05 to 2022-23, raising questions about the alignment of consumption spending with national income growth. This comprehensive data is vital for assessing household well-being, establishing poverty measures, and updating the consumption basket used to calculate the Consumer Price Index, which plays a crucial role in guiding monetary policy.

### [AI's ability to predict death may not be as scary as it sounds](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/ais-ability-to-predict-death-may-not-be-as-scary-as-it-sounds-11709044831270.html)

- Researchers used AI to predict when people would die with 78% accuracy using data on thousands of people in Denmark, but the results were misrepresented and AI cannot predict the exact day of death.

- AI-based systems could have both positive and negative impacts, such as improving lifespan calculations or being used for discrimination.

- The AI technology has limitations: it cannot predict freak accidents or deaths far in advance since predicting the future becomes increasingly difficult the further ahead you go.

- There's a risk of humans trusting AI's predictions blindly due to authority bias, and AI can be influenced by bad studies and flawed data.

- The article emphasizes that our actions can change the future, and these forecasts do not seal our fate as certain events are still subject to change based on our choices.

- Income and job type can affect life expectancy, a correlation recognized even before AI.

### [India’s consumption survey: A significant shift amid modest gains](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-consumption-survey-a-significant-shift-amid-modest-gains-11708958351847.html)

The latest Household Consumption Expenditure Survey (HCES) shows a moderate improvement in Indian consumption patterns over the past decade. Rural Indian households have reduced food expenditure (from 53% to 46.4%) and increased spending on non-food items. While average monthly per capita expenditure has risen in both rural and urban areas, the increase is modest. The survey also indicates a shift towards healthier diets, with increased spending on dairy, eggs, and fresh fruits. The methodology for this HCES round has been revised, but the exact changes are unclear. The survey results could become a political tool during upcoming elections, but they do not provide significant evidence of widespread prosperity or hardship.

### [India’s development landscape has undergone a structural shift](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-development-landscape-has-undergone-a-structural-shift-11708958398028.html)

After an 11-year wait, India has released a Fact Sheet regarding the Household Consumption Expenditure Survey (HCES) for 2022-23. According to the World Bank's extreme poverty line, the percentage of people living in extreme poverty in India has significantly decreased from 12.2% in 2011-12 to only 2% now. This means that extreme poverty has almost been eliminated in India. Using a higher poverty line of PPP $3.2, the poverty rate reduced from 53.6% in 2011-12 to 21% in 2022-23. Additionally, inequality has declined in both rural and urban areas, with rural Gini coefficient dropping from 28.7 to 27.0 and urban Gini coefficient falling from 36.7 to 31.9. This remarkable pro-poor development is attributed to strong growth and reduced inequality under the growth policies of the Narendra Modi government.

### [Chip-maker Taiwan’s electorate has rebuffed Beijing](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/chipmaker-taiwan-s-electorate-has-rebuffed-beijing-11705330507318.html)

Taiwan's recent presidential election resulted in Vice President Lai Ching-te being elected as the island's president, marking the third consecutive win for the independence-leaning Democratic Progressive Party (DPP). However, the DPP lost its narrow legislative majority, limiting Lai's ability to push for Taiwan's independence from mainland China. Taiwan plays a crucial role in global technological leadership, particularly in semiconductor manufacturing. The country is home to over 60% of the world's semiconductor manufacturing and makes over 90% of the most advanced chips. Taiwan's electronics industry also extends beyond semiconductors, with Taiwanese-owned companies in China producing and exporting high-end components. Taiwan's history includes Japanese rule and subsequent control by the KMT (KuoMinTang) party, which led to an uprising and brutal suppression by the KMT in 1947. The KMT later established a dictatorship but focused on developing the economy, especially in electronics and technology. Democratization began in the late 1980s, leading to tensions with Beijing, including missile firings by China during Taiwan's first free presidential election in 1996. The KMT and DPP have different views on Taiwan's status, with the KMT agreeing with China's "One China" policy, while the DPP sees Taiwan as separate from China. In the recent election, all three candidates were native-Taiwanese, reflecting the DPP's identity politics. A stable Taiwan Strait would benefit countries like India, as Taiwanese

### [Combating fake news: Staying away from Google can be a solution](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/combating-fake-news-staying-away-from-google-can-be-a-solution-11705326180610.html)

A recent study published in Nature suggests that people are more likely to be fooled by fake news stories after conducting an internet search. The study found that searching for information often leads people to more bad information, creating a spiral effect. Participants in the study, who predominantly used Google, showed an increase in classifying fake news as fact after conducting online research. The study also revealed that people tend to trust search engines more than mainstream media. Additionally, the study found that certain search methods and approaches, such as relying on specific phrases or trusting certain sources, can contribute to misinformation. Fact checkers, who diligently check the credibility of sources and scan search results before selecting what to read, have an advantage in identifying accurate information. However, even fact checkers do not always agree on the credibility of certain stories. This study serves as a reminder that accessing the truth through a simple online search is not always reliable.

Mon, 15 Jan 2024 23:41:54 +0530
### [Why are we staring at a global debt problem yet again?](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/why-are-we-staring-at-a-global-debt-problem-yet-again-11705326246084.html)

Global public debt reached historical highs in 2023, posing a risk to the world economy's growth. The US and China have public debt-to-GDP ratios exceeding 120% of GDP. Debt has become a constraint for governments unable to meet essential payments, and many low-income and emerging market countries are at high risk of debt distress. The IMF believes the risk of a systemic wave of debt defaults is low, but the outlook is grim. The lack of effective debt resolution instruments and transparency around debt contribute to the problem. A global debt reporting system and improved fiscal data are needed to address these issues.

### [Develop Lakshadweep but only for eco-friendly tourism](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/develop-lakshadweep-but-only-for-eco-friendly-tourism-11704988367255.html)

Maldivian ministers' comments against India caused a diplomatic dispute and led to their removal from power in the Maldives. This incident sparked interest in developing Lakshadweep, a Union territory near Kerala, as an alternative tourist destination. While Lakshadweep and the Maldives share similar appeal as holiday destinations, replicating the high-end resort model on a smaller scale may be challenging. Nevertheless, there is a push for tourism development in Lakshadweep, with plans for a new airport and potential interest from corporations to set up five-star resorts. Prime Minister Narendra Modi's recent visit further fueled anticipation for tourism growth. However, due to limitations in terms of size and infrastructure, Lakshadweep can likely cater only to affluent travelers. It is crucial to prioritize eco-friendly development from the beginning to protect the islands' natural treasures and appeal to the rising eco-consciousness in the world. Lessons should be learned from the Maldives, where increasing tourist arrivals led to waste disposal challenges and environmental degradation. Sustainability surveys and strict adherence to regulations are necessary to prevent similar issues in Lakshadweep. Limiting construction and controlling visitor numbers, while taxing affluent tourists to cover extra expenses, can help maintain the islands' integrity.

### [Truckers’ protests: government mustn’t yield to unreasonable demands](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/truckers-protests-government-mustn-t-yield-to-unreasonable-demands-11704267675164.html)

#### Summary:

The Indian government is facing protests from truckers over new provisions in the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita that increase the penalty for hit-and-run crimes. The provisions replace the Indian Penal Code and include a maximum sentence of 10 years' imprisonment and fines. The government has assured the truckers' union that the new rules will be implemented only after consultation with the transporters' body. The high rate of road fatalities in India, including hit-and-run accidents, is attributed to factors such as mob justice, lack of police accountability, and corruption. The truck drivers are concerned about potential extortion and arbitrary charges. Addressing these issues requires reforming the police and the system of administration. The article also raises questions about mandating cameras in vehicles, police accountability, and human rights watchdogs. Diluting laws without addressing the underlying issues is seen as feeding the dynamic of mob rule.

#### Analysis:

The article discusses the truckers' strike in India against new provisions in the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita that increase the penalty for hit-and-run crimes. The government has assured the truckers' union that the new rules will be implemented only after consultation with the transporters' body [[1]](https://www.thehindu.com/news/national/amid-nationwide-strike-by-drivers-and-transporters-on-increased-punishment-in-hit-and-run-cases-mha-meets-transport-body/article67698427.ece) [[2]](https://www.thehindu.com/news/national/truck-drivers-across-states-protest-centres-new-law-on-hit-and-run-cases/article67697574.ece) The high rate of road fatalities in India is a major concern, with 461,312 road accidents occurring in 2022, resulting in 168,491 deaths [[5]](https://thewire.in/rights/truckers-transporters-protest-10-year-sentence-for-hit-and-run-in-new-criminal-law). The article highlights several reasons for the high rate of hit-and-run accidents in India, including mob justice, lack of police accountability, and corruption The truck drivers are concerned about potential extortion and arbitrary charges, as well as the increased penalties for hit-and-run crimes [[10]](https://www.indiatoday.in/india/story/hit-and-run-law-truckers-drivers-protest-to-be-withdrawn-transport-association-meeting-with-government-2483416-2024-01-02). The article suggests that addressing these issues requires reforming the police and the system of administration [[11]]. It also raises questions about mandating cameras in vehicles, police accountability, and human rights watchdogs [[11]]. Diluting laws without addressing the underlying issues is seen as feeding the dynamic of mob rule [[11]].

#### Conclusion:

The truckers' strike in India is a response to new provisions in the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita that increase the penalty for hit-and-run crimes. The strike highlights concerns about mob justice, lack of police accountability, and corruption in the country. Addressing these issues requires reforming the police and the system of administration. The article also raises questions about mandating cameras in vehicles, police accountability, and human rights watchdogs. Diluting laws without addressing the underlying issues is seen as feeding the dynamic of mob rule.

Wed, 03 Jan 2024 08:00:07 +0530
### [The hullabaloo over crypto has quietened despite the good year it had](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-hullabaloo-over-crypto-has-quietened-despite-the-good-year-it-had-11704205040952.html)

According to an article titled "The Big Crypto SE," Bitcoin experienced a rally of 155% in US dollar terms in 2023. The Bloomberg Galaxy Crypto Index, which represents crypto as an investment asset class, had a return of around 140% during the same year. Despite the impressive performance of crypto as an asset class, there was a lack of fervor for Bitcoin and crypto in general in 2023. The volume of Bitcoin traded was significantly lower compared to previous years, indicating less interest in spite of the price increase. Several factors contribute to this phenomenon.

First, in India, the introduction of a 30% tax on capital gains from buying and selling crypto, along with the inability to offset losses against other gains, has reduced the popularity of cryptocurrencies in the country.

Second, many people who entered the crypto market in 2020 and 2021 experienced losses when Bitcoin and crypto prices peaked in November 2021. This has made them more cautious about investing in crypto again.

Third, the fear of missing out (FOMO) dynamic, which typically drives retail investors to invest in an asset class that has rallied substantially, has shifted to small-cap stocks and financial derivatives in India. Financial influencers who previously promoted crypto have now moved on to these alternative investments, impacting word of mouth.

Fourth, the prevalence of crypto scams and the realization that a significant portion of crypto is owned by a few individuals or "whales" who manipulate prices through circular trading has eroded trust in the industry. Fake trades on unregulated exchanges and cases of crypto exchanges shutting down and investors losing access to their funds have also contributed to the skepticism.

Fifth, despite the hype around the use cases of crypto, no substantial developments have emerged, leading some to view it as an asset with value derived solely from speculation.

Sixth, the media coverage and advertisements promoting crypto have diminished, possibly due to venture capitalist funding running out or the industry being cautious in response to government crackdowns on its unregulated nature.

Seventh, the availability of safer investment options, such as bank fixed deposits with higher interest rates, has reduced the incentive for retail investors to take on the higher risk associated with crypto.

These factors collectively explain the lack of enthusiasm for crypto despite its price surge in 2023.

### [The world should stay vigilant over a debt crisis in the Global South](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-world-should-stay-vigilant-over-a-debt-crisis-in-the-global-south-11704194243185.html)

The International Economic Association (IEA) recently held its 20th World Congress in Medellín, Colombia. The conference brought together economists from around the world to discuss the latest developments in economic thinking. This year's Congress highlighted the need to re-evaluate some of the fundamental assumptions in the field of economics. The escalating debt crisis in the Global South was a significant concern during the conference, although it was not the main focus [[1]](https://www.oecd.org/education/skills-beyond-school/Reviews%20of%20National%20Policies%20for%20Education%20Tertiary%20Education%20in%20Colombia%202012.pdf).

The IEA, founded in 1950, has been led by renowned economists such as Joseph Schumpeter, Paul Samuelson, János Kornai, Kenneth J. Arrow, Amartya Sen, and Joseph E. Stiglitz. The Congress shed light on the challenges faced by the global economy, including supply-chain disruptions due to the war in Ukraine, the lingering effects of the COVID-19 pandemic, and the uncertainty surrounding the conflict between Israel and Hamas [[2]](https://ww2.arb.ca.gov/sites/default/files/2022-05/2022-draft-sp.pdf).

One of the key themes discussed at the Congress was the impact of digital technologies and social media on labor, wages, and inequality. Presentations also focused on the changing nature of globalization, the shift from a unipolar to a multipolar economic order, and the erosion of democratic institutions in the face of populist nationalism.

During the Congress, Danny Quah's lecture highlighted the rapid changes in the global economy. He discussed the shifting center of economic gravity, which has moved from the middle of the Atlantic Ocean in 1980 to the east, driven by the growth of East Asian economies, particularly India and China. Quah projected that by 2050, the world's economic center will settle between India and China, which could lead to geopolitical tensions and new threats [[2]](https://ww2.arb.ca.gov/sites/default/files/2022-05/2022-draft-sp.pdf).

The rise of authoritarianism was identified as a major driver of global economic uncertainty. Populist movements were seen as a potential threat to democratic governance, civil liberties, and the liberal world order. The appeal of these movements can be partly attributed to rising inequality and reduced social mobility.

The article also highlights the potential risks to the global economy, particularly in the developing world. The COVID-19 pandemic has led to increased public spending in many countries, but while developed and middle-income countries had the resources to cope, low- and lower-middle-income economies borrowed heavily, leading to debt distress. The World Bank's International Debt Report indicates that the world's poorest countries have been hit hardest by the sovereign-debt crisis, with some already defaulting and others at high risk of default.

The article emphasizes the need for urgent international intervention to prevent the situation from escalating. Failure to address the developing world's debt crisis could have long-term effects, including exacerbating the migration crisis and fueling the rise of right-wing populism in developed countries. The international community, particularly multilateral institutions like the World Bank, must take decisive action to prevent the situation from spiraling out of control.

In conclusion, the IEA's World Congress highlighted the need to re-evaluate economic assumptions in light of global challenges. The conference focused on the impact of digital technologies, the changing nature of globalization, and the rise of authoritarianism. The article also emphasized the urgent need to address the developing world's debt crisis to prevent long-term consequences for the global economy [[1]](https://www.oecd.org/education/skills-beyond-school/Reviews%20of%20National%20Policies%20for%20Education%20Tertiary%20Education%20in%20Colombia%202012.pdf)

### [The NYT’s copyright lawsuit against OpenAI reveals a familiar but pointless fear](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-nyt-s-copyright-lawsuit-against-openai-reveals-a-familiar-but-pointless-fear-11704205094732.html)

The New York Times filed a lawsuit against OpenAI for copyright infringement, claiming that OpenAI's large language models (LLMs) exhibit "memorization" behavior, allowing users to bypass the New York Times' paywall and access copyrighted content without a subscription. However, the author of an article investigating this claim found that when using ChatGPT, a language model developed by OpenAI, it did not generate verbatim excerpts from the New York Times articles listed in the complaint. Instead, it provided a message stating that it cannot provide verbatim excerpts and suggested visiting the New York Times website for the full article.

The article argues that the New York Times' claim is based on an incorrect understanding of how LLMs work and what copyright law is meant to protect. LLMs do not copy the content they are trained on; instead, they read and parameterize the data into weights in a neural network. This process is different from copying and storing the actual text. The article compares this process to search engines, which crawl the web and generate an index of content without violating copyright law. Courts have recognized search engine activity as permissible under fair use exceptions. The article suggests that the transformation that occurs when LLMs parameterize content is even greater than what search engines do.

The article also speculates that the New York Times' lawsuit may be a negotiating tactic to pressure OpenAI into agreeing to licensing demands. It notes that OpenAI has previously entered into licensing deals with other media companies. The author expresses confusion about why the New York Times sees generative AI as an existential threat to its high-quality journalism, suggesting that LLMs are essentially advanced auto-complete tools that assist in generating content but do not create novel content.

The article concludes by stating that media organizations have historically resisted transformative leaps in technology, such as the printing press and recorded music, out of a fear of disrupting their existing business models. However, embracing new technologies and adapting to change is crucial for survival. The author suggests that the New York Times should focus on its strengths and produce news content that generative AI cannot match, rather than attempting to bend copyright law in its favor.

Overall, the article challenges the New York Times' claims of copyright infringement by OpenAI's LLMs and argues that the lawsuit may be a strategic move rather than a genuine concern about copyright violations.

Tue, 02 Jan 2024 22:59:48 +0530
### [A cost-benefit analysis can help us make New Year's resolutions that’ll be kept](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/a-cost-benefit-analysis-can-help-us-make-new-years-resolutions-that-ll-be-kept-11704194271050.html)

#### Summary of "How to Make New Year's Resolutions That Stick"

The article discusses the challenge of sticking to New Year's resolutions and provides insights on how to make resolutions that are more likely to be successful. It emphasizes the application of economic principles to evaluate the benefits and costs of resolutions, suggesting that breaking down larger goals into smaller, more concrete ones can help in this process. The article also highlights the importance of evaluating marginal benefits and costs, as well as considering opportunity costs and out-of-pocket financial costs associated with the resolutions. It encourages individuals to focus on personal costs and benefits when setting resolutions and predicts that following this advice can increase the likelihood of keeping New Year's resolutions.

The key points from the article are as follows:
- Surveys suggest that about one-third of all Americans outline one or more goals for the New Year, but only about one in ten can stick with them [[1]](https://www.scribbr.com/working-with-sources/how-to-summarize/).
- The first step in making a resolution that will stick is to apply a core principle of economics: do things only when their benefits exceed the costs. This involves breaking down larger and more general goals into smaller and more concrete ones.
- Evaluating marginal benefits and costs, rather than total benefits and costs, is crucial. Breaking goals into small chunks helps in understanding the effects of incremental changes.
- Concrete goals are easier to achieve, and it's important to consider the costs and benefits of each smaller change to identify which goals would actually be beneficial [[1]](https://www.scribbr.com/working-with-sources/how-to-summarize/).
- Opportunity costs, out-of-pocket financial costs, and personal valuation of goals and sacrifices are essential considerations when setting resolutions.
- Focusing on personal costs and benefits when setting resolutions can increase the likelihood of keeping New Year's resolutions.

This summary provides a concise overview of the key insights from the article on making New Year's resolutions that are more likely to be successful.

Tue, 02 Jan 2024 22:53:25 +0530
### [Capital allocation that reaches deserving MSMEs will result in inclusive growth](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/capital-allocation-that-reaches-deserving-msmes-will-result-in-inclusive-growth-11704194314685.html)

The article discusses the opportunities and challenges faced by micro, small, and medium enterprises (MSMEs) in India. MSMEs contribute a significant portion of India's GDP and exports, but they often struggle with limited access to credit and funding. The article emphasizes the importance of qualitative growth for the MSME sector to reach its true potential.

The growth prospects for MSMEs are viewed through three lenses:

1. Customer base expansion: India's economic rise is driven by increased demand. MSMEs face challenges in finding new markets and customers due to information asymmetry and the dominance of a few big players in the export market.

2. Business operation plans: India's infrastructure development, such as the PM Gati Shakti program and National Logistics Policy, can help address logistical problems faced by MSMEs. However, MSMEs still face manufacturing and production challenges that hinder their ability to scale up and build a brand.

3. Boosted employee productivity: India's vast pool of human capital needs to be upskilled and channeled productively. Industry associations should play a more proactive role in employee training to encourage long-term career perspectives and reduce attrition.

The article concludes by highlighting the need for companies to view MSMEs as suppliers, customers, and partners. It emphasizes the importance of growth-oriented partnerships alongside financing. The government, financial sector, industry associations, and sector-specific bodies should collaborate to create an environment that supports MSMEs' growth and helps India achieve its economic goals.

### [Tight liquidity spells deposit rate hikes](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/quick-edit/tight-liquidity-spells-deposit-rate-hikes-11704124007757.html)

Central banks around the world are considering lowering interest rates, but commercial banks in India have been raising deposit rates. The Reserve Bank of India has raised its policy rate by 2.5 percentage points since May 2022 to combat inflation, but this increase has been slow to reach depositors. Banks are facing a liquidity crunch due to tight cash and large outflows from quarterly advance tax payments. To meet credit demand, banks need to attract more deposits. The RBI has kept liquidity conditions tight to restrain demand and cool price pressures, so the deposit rate hikes align with the central bank's policy goal. However, if the RBI begins to cut rates, complications can arise.

### [Specialists are being educated to address youth mental health](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/an-educational-approach-can-help-address-the-youth-mental-health-crisis-11704111490133.html)

Last year, there were concerning reports about the mental health of children and teens in the US, with higher levels of depression, anxiety, and an increase in rates of suicides and eating disorders. However, there is now hope for a novel solution to address this issue. An experiment in Oregon, funded by a $425 million gift from Connie and Steve Ballmer, aims to expand the mental health workforce by creating a new type of mental health provider. These providers, who will have a bachelor's-level degree, will work in community settings to identify struggling kids and offer brief and early interventions to help them. The students enrolled in this program will receive intensive hands-on training on evidence-backed interventions during their last two years of college. They will gain experience in schools and other community settings and will be ready to enter the field upon graduation. The goal is for these providers to offer brief interventions that can prevent some kids from needing more intensive resources, freeing up professionals with advanced degrees to focus on those who need them most [[1]](https://www.justice.gov/crt/case-summaries).

The Oregon experiment is inspired by the successful 'low intensity' mental health workforce model pioneered in the UK. This model involved the establishment of a new type of provider called a "Psychological Well-being Practitioner," who offers brief interventions to struggling adults. If the Oregon experiment proves successful, it could establish a new layer of support for children across the country [[1]](https://www.justice.gov/crt/case-summaries).

To ensure the effectiveness of the program, robust data will need to be collected to demonstrate that the students are having a positive impact on children's mental health. The first cohort of students will enter classrooms in the fall, and anyone who interacts with a Ballmer student will have the opportunity to offer feedback on their experience. This feedback will help assess whether the services provided actually improve kids' mental health [[1]](https://www.justice.gov/crt/case-summaries).

While the experiment in Oregon shows promise, there are practical challenges to overcome. The program has already been approved by the state higher education commission, but working with US policymakers to establish certification standards for child behavioral health specialists and defining the services they can deliver is the next step. Additionally, convincing insurers to recognize the value of the care provided by these new professionals and cover their services will be crucial [[1]](https://www.justice.gov/crt/case-summaries).

If the Oregon experiment proves successful, it could serve as a model for other institutions to adopt a similar approach, helping to establish a new level of support for children's mental health nationwide. While the cost of the Ballmer Institute's experiment is significant, if it demonstrates positive outcomes, it may encourage other institutions to invest in similar initiatives to address the mental health crisis among children and teens

### [Four major elections and a rate cut: What to watch out for in 2024](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/four-major-elections-and-a-rate-cut-2024-will-be-an-exciting-year-11704111458536.html)

According to the article, several developments are expected to shape the global economy in the first quarter of 2024. The ongoing war in Ukraine and the humanitarian crisis in the Levant are likely to continue, impacting the world economy. The US economy may avoid a recession, while the Eurozone will continue to search for economic growth. Global central banks might also loosen their hold on monetary policy. However, the key to global economic prospects in 2024 will be domestic politics.

Over 50 national elections are expected to take place in 2024, with four of them being critical for the global economy: the US, Russia, the EU, and India. The US presidential election will be closely watched, with Donald Trump attempting a comeback despite legal and regulatory challenges. If Trump wins, certain economic outcomes can be predicted, such as climate denial, withdrawal from multilateral agreements, and increased protectionism. If Trump is barred from contesting, the US economy's trajectory will play a significant role.

In Russia, Vladimir Putin's re-election as president is seen as a foregone conclusion. This could have economic repercussions, and a true alternative emerging through free and fair elections could lead to a more favorable impact on the global economy. In the Eurozone, growth is expected to remain elusive, and the emergence of right-wing leaders may result in tighter immigration barriers, higher trade-protection walls, and lower climate ambitions.

India's general elections, likely to be held in April or May, will see a shift in government expenditure patterns from capital expenditure to consumption. Political parties are expected to compete in offering welfare benefits, and India's economic growth is forecasted to slow down marginally during 2024-25. Balancing a runaway capital market with slowing consumption demand will be a challenge for India.

The timing of rate cuts by central banks is expected to influence domestic politics in countries with national elections in 2024. The US Federal Reserve and the European Central Bank are anticipated to start cutting rates around June 2024. The path chosen by the Reserve Bank of India (RBI) will be interesting to observe, as it usually implements rate actions after the Fed's meetings.

China's role in global geopolitical shifts and Japan's potential rise as it raises interest rates out of negative territory are identified as two unpredictable factors for 2024.

In summary, 2024 is expected to be an exciting year with significant political events and potential economic surprises.

### [HUL signals first steps to regain market share from small players](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/hul-signals-first-steps-to-regain-market-share-from-small-players-11704083058272.html)

Hindustan Unilever (HUL), the largest fast-moving consumer goods (FMCG) manufacturer in India, has made changes to its distributor margins in an attempt to stimulate volumes and reduce distribution costs. The company has shifted from a fixed margin model to an increased variable margin across various distributor categories.

HUL has acknowledged a decline in its value market share, particularly in the mass-end of its portfolio, losing ground to smaller competitors. The CEO & MD of HUL, Rohit Jawa, mentioned the resurgence of small and regional players in select categories and price points as a contributing factor to this decline.

A recent survey by Redseer indicates that a significant portion of consumers are open to purchasing unbranded products if they meet the criteria of quality and perceived value.

The trend among mass consumers is shifting towards utilizing e-commerce platforms for a wide range of shopping categories, including FMCG. Direct-to-consumer (D2C) brands are offering attractive pricing and product variety, which might provide valuable marketing insights for FMCG brands.

Prominent FMCG companies, including HUL, are experiencing a decline in pricing growth. This shift is attributed to adjustments in trade pipelines and the integration of product price reductions by companies, which is now becoming evident in pushing for retail sales, according to a Nielsen report [[5]](https://www.hul.co.in/files/92ui5egz/production/8a1b3f103408328781a6ebf434b8e5172e4bfc91.pdf).

Analysts anticipate gradual improvement in volume growth for most FMCG firms, including HUL. Gross margins have shown a sequential recovery, attributed to the stability of key raw material prices.

However, HUL faces the challenge of local and regional competitors. Ebitda margins have exhibited a measured recovery, influenced by increased advertising expenditures aimed at enhancing market presence. Larger players like HUL are expected to encounter a more subdued pace of volume growth.

While HUL's stock price has remained unchanged for over two years, its counterparts have demonstrated more favorable performance. The FMCG sector experienced growth in 2023, with the Nifty FMCG index surpassing the benchmark.

To fortify its position against local and regional competitors, HUL needs to establish brand attractiveness and entice distributors to drive volume growth. Introducing new product lines, particularly in the beauty and well-being segment, may be crucial for capturing consumer attention and boosting sales.

In conclusion, HUL is making changes to its distributor margins in an effort to stimulate volumes and reduce distribution costs. The company is facing challenges from smaller competitors and the shift towards e-commerce platforms. To sustain market relevance, HUL needs to focus on brand attractiveness, introduce new product lines, and enhance its digital agenda

### [Geopolitics is leading us to fragmentation. Can it be stopped?](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/columns/geopolitics-is-leading-us-to-fragmentation-can-it-be-stopped-11704041370903.html)

#### Summary of "Geopolitical Pressures and the Global Economy"

The global economy is facing fragmentation due to geopolitical pressures and non-economic factors, which could have significant implications for economic stability, growth, and efforts to combat climate change. The primary catalyst of this fragmentation is heightened geopolitical tensions, particularly the escalating rivalry between the United States and China. China's emergence as the world's largest economy and the decline in US manufacturing jobs have fueled discontent with globalization and reshaped views on China. President Xi Jinping's move towards a state-centric system controlled by the Communist Party of China has defied expectations of democratization through increased trade. The US response to these developments, including the trade war initiated by former President Donald Trump and maintained by President Joe Biden, reflects a broader geopolitical strategy. The European Union has also embraced a vision of "strategic autonomy" to protect key sectors and reduce reliance on hostile countries. However, this strategy carries risks, as China could retaliate by restricting exports of essential raw materials. Sanctions on Russia led by the US and the EU have reshaped regional trade patterns, contributing to the segmentation of the global economy. The use of national currencies for invoicing exports to Russia has increased, potentially eroding the dominance of the US dollar. Overall, economic fragmentation driven by geopolitical factors is expected to be expensive and negatively affect almost every country in the world, posing a grave threat to planetary health and humanity's future in the midst of a climate emergency.

**Key Points:**
- Geopolitical pressures and non-economic factors are driving the global economy towards fragmentation.
- Heightened geopolitical tensions, particularly between the US and China, are a primary catalyst of this fragmentation.
- The US response includes a trade war with China and a broader geopolitical strategy, while the EU has embraced a vision of "strategic autonomy."
- Sanctions on Russia have reshaped regional trade patterns, contributing to the segmentation of the global economy.
- Economic fragmentation driven by geopolitical factors is expected to be expensive and negatively affect almost every country in the world, posing a grave threat to planetary health and humanity's future in the midst of a climate emergency.

### [The term 'emerging markets' gives no joy. Retire it, heeding Dani Rodrik](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-term-emerging-markets-gives-no-joy-retire-it-heeding-dani-rodrik-11703916311782.html)

Economist Dani Rodrik recently expressed his desire for the term "emerging markets" to be retired. He argues that this term reduces a large part of the world to potential investment targets, overlooking their complexity and internal challenges. While the term may be useful for those managing large pools of savings, such as pension funds and sovereign wealth funds, it fails to consider political differences, macroeconomic conditions, and economic structures specific to each country. For example, it groups authoritarian China with democratic India, despite their significant differences. Rodrik suggests that the categorization of countries as advanced, emerging, or the rest shares a lineage with Eurocentricism and Orientalism, which can have material effects on the non-rich world. The term "emerging markets" also fails to consider the impact of rich-world policies on developing economies. Rodrik's critique of the term should be nuanced, as some professionals of Indian origin in global finance have insights into the complexity of India's economy. Retiring the term may foster empathy among policymakers in advanced economies towards these economies. [[3]](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-term-emerging-markets-gives-no-joy-retire-it-heeding-dani-rodrik-11703916311782.html)

### [Need tighter regulations as India's middle class turns to biz loans](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/need-tighter-regulations-as-indias-middle-class-turns-to-biz-loans-11703657267909.html)

According to an article titled "Need tighter regulations as India's middle class turns to biz loans," a survey conducted by Home Credit in 2023 reveals some concerning trends in borrowing in India. The survey, which included 1,842 borrowers aged 18-55 years across 17 cities, found that while there is a rise in household debt, Indian borrowers have a limited understanding of finances and data privacy rules. Only 18% of the borrowers claimed to understand data privacy rules, and over 60% expressed concerns about how personal data is collected and used. Gen Z borrowers showed higher concern about data privacy, with 70% of them wanting more transparent communication on data usage. The survey also highlighted that consumer goods, such as smartphones and household appliances, accounted for nearly 44% of loans, while 19% of loans were for launching or expanding businesses. There is a growing acceptance of online and digital channels, with 29% of borrowers opting for online loans and 51% showing interest in digital borrowing in the future. Loans initiated through tele-calling increased to 19% in 2023, but loans through POS transactions or bank branches saw a decline. The survey also revealed that 48% of borrowers engage in online shopping, and over 50% prefer app-based loan applications. The preferred loan format for 49% of borrowers is EMI on cards. The article also mentions that the Reserve Bank of India (RBI) has expressed concerns about household borrowing and has increased risk weights on many loan categories. The latest RBI data shows that households are borrowing more and saving less, with financial assets shrinking to the lowest level in almost 50 years. The article suggests that while there are risks associated with high indebtedness and lower savings, the significant portion of borrowing for businesses indicates a risk-taking, entrepreneurial spirit within the middle class. The article emphasizes the need for tighter regulations to protect borrowers from online scams and misleading marketing by lenders. It also suggests that the RBI and other regulators should focus on financial education and designing courses on financial literacy to address the lack of understanding among borrowers. The article concludes by stating that borrowing for business can accelerate future macro-economic growth, and regulators should aim to prevent malpractices in this space while ensuring transparency in the retail credit market.

### [Women’s vote achieved in 2023: Let’s accelerate progress](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/womens-vote-achieved-in-2023-let-s-accelerate-progress-11703777576863.html)

In October 2023, Pope Francis made a historic decision to allow women to vote at the Synod of Bishops for the first time. Previously, women were only allowed to attend as observers. This move marked a significant shift for the male-dominated Roman Catholic Church and made Vatican City the last country in the world to give women the right to vote [[1]](https://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2023/12/29/pope-francis-vatican-top-stories-2023-246802).

The article highlights that the addition of women's voting rights at the Synod of Bishops is a culmination of a democratic quest for justice that has been ongoing for over a century. It acknowledges that religious institutions, like the Catholic Church, often take longer to reform but can and do change over time. The article emphasizes the importance of gender equality in collective decision-making and criticizes patriarchal politics for hindering progress [[2]](https://www.vatican.va/archive/hist_councils/ii_vatican_council/documents/vat-ii_cons_19651207_gaudium-et-spes_en.html).

The women's suffrage movement began in the 19th and early 20th centuries, with protests and activism demanding the right to vote. New Zealand became the first nation to grant women the right to vote in national elections in 1893, followed by the United States in 1920. The article mentions that the need for women's voices to be heard gained urgency after World War I. Over time, more countries granted women the right to vote, although some tried to impose restrictions based on race, age, education level, or marital status [[2]](https://www.vatican.va/archive/hist_councils/ii_vatican_council/documents/vat-ii_cons_19651207_gaudium-et-spes_en.html).

While the article acknowledges the progress made in granting women the right to vote, it also emphasizes the need for proper representation of women in rule-making and governance. It argues that democracy is most effective when it captures and acts upon the desires of all people, regardless of gender or other identities. The article concludes by stating that the political agency of women still has a long way to go before it can be said to have made the world a better place, and calls for continued progress in achieving gender equality [[2]](https://www.vatican.va/archive/hist_councils/ii_vatican_council/documents/vat-ii_cons_19651207_gaudium-et-spes_en.html).

In summary, the article discusses Pope Francis' decision to allow women to vote at the Synod of Bishops, highlighting the significance of this move for the Roman Catholic Church and Vatican City. It also provides a brief overview of the women's suffrage movement and emphasizes the importance of gender equality in democratic processes and decision-making [[1]](https://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2023/12/29/pope-francis-vatican-top-stories-2023-246802) [[2]](https://www.vatican.va/archive/hist_councils/ii_vatican_council/documents/vat-ii_cons_19651207_gaudium-et-spes_en.html).

Thu, 28 Dec 2023 23:39:24 +0530

The article discusses the recent state elections in India and the factors that influence voting behavior. It argues that drawing conclusions about the relative performance of states based on election results may not yield fair conclusions. The campaigns in these elections focused on various benefits promised by political parties, including direct cash transfers, free bus tickets for women, revival of old pension schemes, and subsidies on cooking gas and housing. The article highlights that while these schemes have their merits, there is a concern about their relative priority compared to government expenditure on investment and other key programs. The rush for cash transfers as a solution to every problem in the economy and society may not be the best way to spur growth or redistribution.

**Key Points:**
- Incumbent governments in all states except Madhya Pradesh lost in the recent state elections in India.
- Economic performance is an important factor influencing voting behavior, but not the sole one.
- Drawing conclusions about the relative performance of states based on election results may not be fair.
- The campaigns in these elections focused on various benefits promised by political parties, including direct cash transfers, free bus tickets for women, revival of old pension schemes, and subsidies on cooking gas and housing.
- While these schemes have their merits, there is a concern about their relative priority compared to government expenditure on investment and other key programs.
- The rush for cash transfers as a solution to every problem in the economy and society may not be the best way to spur growth or redistribution.

### [Dry January too daunting? A damp one is also worthwhile](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/dry-january-too-daunting-a-damp-one-is-also-worthwhile-11703765997549.html)

According to an article, "Dry January" is a campaign that encourages people to abstain from alcohol for the month of January. However, data from Morning Consult suggests that fewer people in the US participated in Dry January in 2023, with older generations showing the least interest. The article suggests that instead of complete abstinence, a "damp" January, where individuals consume less alcohol, can still offer health benefits. Reflecting on one's relationship with alcohol and taking inventory of how the body feels on less booze are some of the benefits of a moderate approach to alcohol consumption in January. The article also emphasizes the importance of self-regulation and setting goals for moderation. It cautions against substituting alcohol with THC-infused drinks, as the effects of THC on the body are different and less comprehensively studied than alcohol. The article concludes that taking a break from alcohol, whether completely or in moderation, can have long-lasting benefits for one's health.

**Key Points:**
- Fewer people in the US participated in Dry January in 2023, with older generations showing the least interest.
- A "damp" January, where individuals consume less alcohol, can still offer health benefits.
- Reflecting on one's relationship with alcohol and taking inventory of how the body feels on less booze are some of the benefits of a moderate approach to alcohol consumption in January.
- Self-regulation, setting goals, and monitoring progress are important for a successful dry or damp January.
- Substituting alcohol with THC-infused drinks is not recommended, as the effects of THC on the body are different and less comprehensively studied than alcohol.
- Taking a break from alcohol, whether completely or in moderation, can have long-lasting benefits for one's health

### [How magicians control flip of a coin](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/columns/how-magicians-control-flip-of-a-coin-11703779854563.html)

According to an article titled "Fair Coins Tend to Land on the Same Side They Started: Evidence from 350,757 Flips" by František Bartoš and others, the researchers conducted an experiment involving 48 participants who tossed coins a total of 350,757 times. The goal of the experiment was to test the hypothesis that a flipped coin tends to land on the same side it started with more often than chance would suggest. The researchers found that while the overall percentage of heads and tails was close to 50%, the coins landed on the same side they started with slightly more often than expected, with a percentage of 50.77%. This finding supports a previous study by mathematician Persi Diaconis and colleagues, who concluded that a coin's starting position can influence its final landing position. However, it is important to note that the bias observed in the experiment was very slight and would require a large number of tosses to detect. The article highlights the role of precession and the initial conditions of the coin's flight in contributing to this bias. Overall, the experiment provides evidence that there is a slight tendency for a flipped coin to land on the same side it started with, but the effect is minimal and not significant enough to rely on for making accurate predictions.

### [Why Paytm’s long search for consistent profits continues](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/why-paytm-s-long-search-for-consistent-profits-continues-11703746933012.html)

Paytm, an online payments platform, recently announced its plans to build an AI system to assist financial institutions in identifying risks and frauds [[2]](https://www.techcircle.in/2023/08/22/paytm-building-ai-system-to-enable-financial-institutions-capture-possible-risks-ceo/). The company aims to safeguard these institutions from emerging threats associated with advancements in AI. At the same time, Paytm is automating repetitive tasks and promoting AI adoption among its employees, resulting in the layoff of over 1,000 employees since October.

Paytm claims that the implementation of AI has exceeded their expectations and has resulted in cost savings of 10-15% in employee costs The company also stated that it evaluates cases of non-performance throughout the year.

While Paytm remains strong in the payments sector, it lacks a coherent business strategy and has yet to demonstrate which business it plans to build over time to deliver consistent profits The company launched its digital wealth-management product, Paytm Money, in 2018, which has performed moderately well in the mutual fund business. However, it faces competition from global and domestic banks as well as other specialized wealth-management platforms.

Paytm has shown inconsistency in its approach to insurance. In September, the company announced that it would not enter the insurance market after failing to conclude a deal for QBE Raheja Insurance. However, it has now changed its decision and stated that insurance and wealth will be a logical expansion of its platform.

The recent regulatory measures by the Reserve Bank of India (RBI) to tackle unsecured lending may impact Paytm's profitable lending segment involving loans under ₹50,000, which could affect its revenues [[3]](https://www.icmrindia.org/casestudies/catalogue/IT%20and%20Systems/ITSY105.htm).

In light of these challenges, the announcement of new business lines by Paytm may be seen as an attempt to maintain a positive image and stock price. Shareholders and stock watchers may demand a more coherent strategy from the company and hold its management and board accountable.

Macquarie, in a research report, expressed concerns about Paytm's lack of focus and its inability to become a category leader in any business except wallets. The rise of UPI payments has made wallets inconsequential, and competition and regulation may impact the company's growth prospects in the medium term [[3]](https://www.icmrindia.org/casestudies/catalogue/IT%20and%20Systems/ITSY105.htm).

Overall, Paytm is still struggling to find its focus and prove its ability to deliver consistent profits

According to the article, the author predicts that small and medium enterprise (SME) stocks listed on the BSE SME exchange will experience a significant bust in 2024. The author highlights the strong performance of SME stocks in recent years, with the BSE SME IPO index generating a return of 2,495% over the previous five years, compared to the relatively lower returns of the BSE Sensex and BSE Smallcap indices [[1]](https://scottaaronson.blog/?p=7094).

However, the author also points out that the price-to-earnings multiple of the BSE SME index is significantly higher than that of the BSE Sensex and BSE Smallcap indices, indicating a potential overvaluation of SME stocks. The author attributes this to the enthusiasm of investors in the SME market and the excessive amount of money flowing into these stocks [[1]](https://scottaaronson.blog/?p=7094).

The article further highlights the oversubscription of SME IPOs, with examples such as Benchmark Computer Solutions, Siyaram Recycling, S J Logistics, Accent Microcell, Deepak Chemtex, and Net Avenue Tech being oversubscribed by significant multiples. The author suggests that this oversubscription and the euphoria surrounding SME stocks could lead to a scenario where investors could take a massive hit if something goes wrong. Additionally, the relatively shallow volumes of the SME stock exchange could result in illiquid shares in a collapsing market.

The author provides examples of individual SME stocks, such as Deepak Chemtex and AMIC Forging, to illustrate the potential risks and rewards associated with investing in SME stocks. These examples show that while some stocks have experienced significant losses, others have seen substantial gains. The author emphasizes that the SME market segment appears to be a lottery market, where even if investors guess the right numbers, they still need another miracle to turn paper profits into real profits by being able to exit their positions [[1]](https://scottaaronson.blog/?p=7094).

In conclusion, the article warns investors to tread with caution when considering investing in SME stocks. The author suggests consulting a personal investment advisor or wealth manager before making any decisions

### [All the world's a stage and we got to play unexpected parts in 2023](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/all-the-worlds-a-stage-and-we-got-to-play-unexpected-parts-in-2023-11703679901340.html)

The article reflects on the top 10 developments of 2023. Here is a summary of the key points:

#### 1. Economists' Predictions:
The article mentions that economists' predictions for a doomsday scenario in the global economy did not materialize. The world economy turned out to be stronger than expected, leading to a soft-landing instead of a hard-landing [[1]](https://www.vcestudyguides.com/blog/station-eleven-by-emily-st-john-mandel).

#### 2. Collapse of Silicon Valley Bank:
The collapse of Silicon Valley Bank (SVB) in the US, along with other banks like Signature Bank and Silvergate Bank, due to over-investment in US Treasury bonds is discussed. This event led to discussions about the differences between the US and India's banking systems [[1]](https://www.vcestudyguides.com/blog/station-eleven-by-emily-st-john-mandel).

#### 3. US Debt Ceiling and Shutdown Concerns:
The article mentions the concerns about the US hitting its debt ceiling and the possibility of a government shutdown. Although it was unlikely to happen, the downgrading of the US's sovereign credit rating by Fitch led to discussions about de-dollarization and its impact on India [[1]](https://www.vcestudyguides.com/blog/station-eleven-by-emily-st-john-mandel).

#### 4. Discussions on De-dollarization:
Discussions on de-dollarization shifted to how the Indian rupee could replace the dollar. India's growing economy and agreements with other countries to use the rupee were seen as steps towards internationalizing the currency. However, these discussions have been ongoing for several years.

#### 5. Indian Bonds in JPMorgan Bond Index:
The inclusion of Indian bonds in the JPMorgan bond index was seen as a positive development. Estimates varied on the amount of foreign investment that would flow into India as a result.

#### 6. Israel-Hamas War and Oil Price Projections:
The Israel-Hamas war led to projections about oil prices, despite neither Israel nor Palestinian territories being major oil producers. The impact on India's economy, including fuel subsidies and inflation, was discussed [[1]](https://www.vcestudyguides.com/blog/station-eleven-by-emily-st-john-mandel).

#### 7. G20 Summit:
The G20 summit generated hype and discussions, but it is unclear what substantive gains were made. The author questions the actual impact of the summit.

#### 8. Withdrawal of ₹2,000 Notes:
The withdrawal of ₹2,000 notes sparked memories of demonetization in the past. The article raises questions about the motives behind the withdrawal and speculates about the future of the ₹500 note [[1]](https://www.vcestudyguides.com/blog/station-eleven-by-emily-st-john-mandel).

#### 9. Incorrect Social Media Post on India's GDP:
A social media post claiming that India's GDP had crossed the $4 trillion mark created excitement, but it was later revealed to be incorrect. The article highlights the need for accurate data and cautions against relying solely on social media for news.

#### 10. GDP Growth and Manufacturing:
India's second-quarter GDP growth for 2023-24 exceeded expectations, with manufacturing showing significant growth. The article points out that GDP growth can occur even when sales in certain sectors decline, as long as profits increase.

In conclusion, the article reflects on various economic and geopolitical developments in 2023, highlighting both positive and questionable aspects.

### [Investors may need to take foot off the small-cap segment in 2024](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/columns/investors-may-need-to-take-foot-off-the-small-cap-segment-in-2024-11703694778524.html)

In 2023, India experienced several developments that boosted investor confidence and led to new highs in market indices. Here are some key highlights from the article:

#### Manufacturing Sector
- The Purchasing Managers' Index (PMI) for November 2023 rose to 56, indicating expansion in factory production.
- New orders increased, and exports continued to rise for the 20th consecutive month.
- Eight main sectors, including coal, oil, natural gas, steel, cement, and electricity, contribute significantly to the Index of Industrial Production (IIP).

#### Production-Linked Incentives (PLI)
- Post-pandemic, various PLI schemes have been announced for the manufacturing sector in India.
- Efforts to strengthen infrastructure, connectivity, and streamline bureaucracy have encouraged multinational corporations (MNCs) to invest more in India.
- India could benefit from outsourcing manufacturing in electronic components such as printed circuit boards and equipment cases.

#### Electronic Manufacturing Services Sector
- The Indian electronic manufacturing services sector is expected to grow at a compounded annual growth rate (CAGR) of 32% from 2021 to 2026.
- The government aims to fulfill 70% of India's IT hardware demand through domestic manufacturing, reducing reliance on imports.

#### National Single Window System
- India has been positioned as a leader in global trade facilitation efforts, achieving a score of 93.55% in 2023, compared to 90.32% in 2021, according to a survey by the United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia Pacific (UNESCAP).

#### Buoyancy of Domestic Investors
- Despite geopolitical volatility, Indian investors remained optimistic due to political stability, strong corporate earnings, and a positive economic outlook.
- Net inflows of ₹233,518 crore were observed in equity funds until November 30, 2023, supported by an increasing Systematic Investment Plan (SIP) book.

#### Potential for Growth
- India has significant potential for growth, with per capita income at $2,450 compared to $12,540 in China and less than one-tenth of the average for countries in the Organization for Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD).
- The addition of new income tax payers indicates the emergence of new potential investors [[1]](https://www.imf.org/-/media/Files/Publications/WEO/2022/April/English/text.ashx).

#### Small- and Mid-Cap Performance
- The small- and mid-cap (SMID) space in India performed well in 2023, attracting ₹58,000 crore of net inflows.
- The significance of SMID has increased over the years, and valuation in this space may appear stretched compared to large caps.

#### Investment Strategies
- Investors with a moderate risk profile and a tilt towards mid- and small-cap mutual funds may consider rebalancing by adding large-cap funds to their portfolio.
- Conservative investors can explore opportunities provided by debt funds, especially short-term duration funds.

In summary, India's manufacturing sector, production-linked incentives, electronic manufacturing services, trade facilitation efforts, domestic investor confidence, and growth potential are key factors contributing to the country's economic development in 2023.
