GPT-3.5: India has a long and strong history of capital markets, with the Bombay Stock Exchange being founded in 1875. In the last 10 years, there has been a fundamental change in the nature of India's equity markets. The "Mutual Fund Sahi Hai" campaign launched by the Association of Mutual Funds in India (Amfi) in 2017 has been a significant game changer, leading to an increase of more than 5 million retail investors in mutual funds in its first year. This campaign has helped to boost domestic retail investment in the markets, reducing the dependence on foreign capital. Additionally, Indian pension funds have also started investing in equity markets, providing a solid source of long-term institutional capital. This combination of retail and institutional investment has created a stable and consistent flow of funding into the equity markets, which has helped to withstand foreign outflows during global events. ### [Quantum computing will make online heists likelier than we can fathom](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/quantum-computing-will-make-online-heists-likelier-than-we-can-fathom-11702986422980.html)

Quantum computing poses a potential threat to the security provided by prime numbers in encryption. While traditional computers struggle to decipher large prime numbers, quantum computers have the potential to break down complex ciphers more efficiently. By 2030, it is estimated that a $1 billion quantum computer could break widely used 2048-bit encryption. This could compromise the security of interbank payments and digital signatures, leading to potential scams and theft. The development of quantum-safe cryptography is crucial to ensure the protection of payment instruments and maintain privacy in digital transactions. However, the integration of quantum-safe cryptography may come with increased costs and slower transaction speeds. Further experimentation and research are needed to address these challenges and ensure the security of future payment systems.

The debt crisis in low-income countries has been a persistent issue, and the international policy community has been struggling to address it effectively. The number of economies in debt distress has been on the rise, especially after the expiration of the Debt Service Suspension Initiative (DSSI) at the end of 2021. The Common Framework for Debt Treatments was introduced to facilitate restructuring agreements between countries with unsustainable debts and their creditors, but progress has been slow. The recent agreement between Zambia and its creditors was seen as a breakthrough, but it ultimately collapsed due to concerns about the treatment of different creditors. Overall, the situation calls for a comprehensive approach to resolving the developing-country debt crisis, considering the role of creditors, the need for sustainable relief, and the potential risks of future shocks.

The ruling asserts that unstamped or insufficiently stamped agreements will still be enforceable, with courts deferring the examination of stamp duty sufficiency to arbitrators. ### [Why Shivraj Chouhan could be a good fit as India’s food and agriculture minister](https://www.livemint.com/politics/why-shivraj-chouhan-could-be-a-good-fit-as-india-s-food-and-agriculture-minister-11702449439515.html)

During Shivraj Singh Chouhan's tenure as the chief minister of Madhya Pradesh, agriculture in the state underwent a significant transformation. The agriculture GDP grew at an average rate of 7% per year, surpassing the national average. The farm sector now contributes nearly 44% of the state's GDP, and around 60% of the population is engaged in farming. Chouhan implemented various measures to enhance farm productivity, such as providing power connections to farms, which improved groundwater irrigation. This led to a significant increase in the net area irrigated under canals. The state also focused on maintenance to maximize the utilization of existing infrastructure. As a result, irrigation coverage increased to 81.5%. This improved irrigation allowed farmers to cultivate the same land multiple times a year, leading to an increase in the gross cropped area. The state government also established procurement infrastructure and started paying a bonus over and above the minimum support price for wheat. Wheat procurement in Madhya Pradesh increased significantly, surpassing Punjab. The state government also encourages farmers to diversify into high-value horticulture and dairy farming. Additionally, the government provides cash transfers and schemes to support farming families. Shivraj Singh Chouhan's experience and success in the agriculture sector could be valuable in strengthening India's agriculture sector and modernizing the food policy framework.

Hmm, based on the provided text, it seems that the Indian stock market has experienced a change in direction since the end of October. The BSE Sensex, which is India's premier stock market index, has risen by approximately 9% during this period. This change in direction can be attributed to the behavior of foreign institutional investors (FIIs). In September and October, FIIs sold stocks worth ₹39,316 crore, but from November 1st to December 12th, they have bought stocks worth ₹40,372 crore. Additionally, domestic institutional investors have continued to buy stocks, offsetting the FII sales. The falling yield on the 10-year US Treasury bond since the end of October may have influenced the behavior of FIIs. As the bond market discounts the possibility of inflation being under control in the US and the US Federal Reserve cutting interest rates, FIIs are seeking higher returns and investing in Indian stocks. This has led to a rally in large-cap and mid-cap stocks, as well as a significant rise in the price of small-cap stocks. The valuations of small-cap stocks, measured by their price-to-earnings (PE) ratios, have reached very high levels. It is worth noting that retail investors have been showing interest in small-cap stocks, with net inflows into small-cap mutual funds. However, it is important for investors to diversify their investments across different categories of stocks and avenues to mitigate risks.

The Indian government has banned the use of sugarcane juice and sugar syrup for ethanol production this year due to fears of a drop in sugar output. ### [Here’s an ‘officious’ list of 10 principles for regulators](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/heres-an-officious-list-of-10-principles-for-regulators-11701875772730.html)

This article discusses principles for regulators based on a re-reading of Machiavelli's book, "The Prince." The author emphasizes the importance of regulators understanding and protecting the interests of their primary constituency. They should establish listening posts to gather feedback and opinions from relevant stakeholders. The selection of advisors should be done carefully, considering personal motivations. Policy pronouncements must be well-formulated and amended cautiously. The regulator should encourage open interactions within the organization to foster collaboration. Building a strong and modern team is crucial, as their reputation reflects that of the regulator. Preserving confidentiality is essential in handling sensitive information. The regulator must exercise discrimination when considering advice and suggestions. While change is necessary, policies should not be modified without careful evaluation. The focus of the regulator should be on effectiveness and efficiency rather than popularity. It should possess investigative and enforcement powers and use modern technology to detect fraud. Finally, the regulator should be respected and feared by delivering on promises and taking action against misconduct.

### [Why are retail investors obsessed with IPOs?](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/why-are-retail-investors-obsessed-with-ipos-11701788112222.html)

The article discusses the phenomenon of retail investors chasing initial public offerings (IPOs) in the stock market for listing day gains. It highlights two recent IPOs, Tata Technologies and Zomato, to illustrate how retail investors often get excited about the potential gains but fail to consider the bigger picture.

In the case of Tata Technologies, the IPO was subscribed around 16.5 times, meaning investors received two shares for every 33 they applied for on average. While those who managed to sell their shares at the listing price of ₹1,200 made a profit of 140%, this gain didn't significantly change their lives. Similarly, with Zomato's IPO, despite the share price opening at a premium of over 51% on the listing day, many retail investors didn't receive any allotment or made only small gains.

The article emphasizes that the chance of getting an allotment in an IPO is inversely proportional to its demand. Even if the share price lists at a high premium, the absolute gains made are often not significant. Additionally, not all IPOs that open with great fanfare deliver long-term returns. Examples like Reliance Power's IPO and Infosys' IPO are mentioned to highlight cases where short-term gains turned into losses or missed opportunities.

The article concludes by providing insights for retail investors. It suggests that IPOs are not the only opportunity to invest in a company's stock, and genuine wealth creation often happens from purchases made after the IPO. It advises investors to gradually accumulate stocks they believe have good potential instead of making large purchases at once. Lastly, it reminds readers about the importance of understanding when to consider absolute numbers versus percentages in investment decisions.

### [The spatial spread of economic activities must be mapped for data accuracy](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-spatial-spread-of-economic-activities-must-be-mapped-for-data-accuracy-11701690655546.html)

The article discusses the issue of regional inequality in India and the neglect of local statistical capacity. It highlights the disparities in economic outcomes between different regions and states, emphasizing the lack of tracking and public release of data on regional contributions to national totals. The historical background of statistical development in India is mentioned, including the limited estimates of provincial income in the mid-20th century and the subsequent focus on state income estimation after independence. However, the methods and sources used vary across states, leading to the demand for comparable state domestic product (SDP) estimates by the Planning Commission and Finance Commission. The article also points out the challenges faced by directorates of economics and statistics (DES), such as lack of attention and funding, resulting in dependence on the Union ministry of statistics and programme implementation (Mospi). Recent surveys and the economic census are discussed, with the involvement of Common Service Centres (CSC) raising concerns over data quality. The controversy surrounding the 2015 base-year revision and the Dholakia committee report recommending a bottom-up approach for estimating state and national incomes are mentioned. The need for support from Mospi and state secretariats, as well as external experts, is highlighted to improve the quality of data generated by DES staff. The article concludes by urging states to acknowledge the crisis in their statistical systems and take steps to revamp them, referring to the setup of a statistical task force in Madhya Pradesh as an example.

### [Movie makers: Brace for the gathering storm](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/content-creators-small-and-big-should-brace-for-worsening-headwinds-11700656233037.html)

Porter's Five Forces model is a valuable tool for analyzing industry structure and predicting changes. It assesses the bargaining power of buyers and suppliers, the threat of substitutes and new entrants, and the level of competitive intensity within an industry. By understanding these forces, one can determine the economic attractiveness of a company or industry. In the content creation industry in India, there have been significant changes with the rise of OTT platforms and individual content creators. However, traditional content creators are facing challenges due to consolidation among buyers and the shifting bargaining power. For example, the merger of PVR and Inox has given them a significant share of box office collections, which may lead to increased pressure on film producers. Similarly, the consolidation of satellite rights buyers may also shift bargaining power away from movie producers. Additionally, OTT platforms, after experiencing a surge in viewership during the pandemic, are now being more cautious with content acquisition spending. This may impact small and independent content producers. Overall, the changing dynamics in the content creation industry in India may result in an exodus of independent producers and potential price deflation throughout the movie-making chain. Porter's Five Forces model remains a powerful tool to analyze and understand these shifts.

### [Will Javier Milei dare dollarize Argentina?](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/quick-edit/will-javier-milei-dare-dollarize-argentina-11700575858931.html)

Javier Milei, an economic disruptor and self-described "anarcho-capitalist," has won the presidency in Argentina. He plans to implement a radical agenda, which includes reducing the number of ministries, decreasing public spending, privatizing state enterprises, and eliminating levies and regulatory controls. However, his most audacious proposals involve abolishing the central bank, known for printing pesos at the request of politicians, and adopting the US dollar as the country's currency to combat high inflation. The feasibility of Milei's approach is uncertain due to the lack of legislative support and Argentina's financial constraints. The country owes a significant debt to the International Monetary Fund and has negative net foreign exchange reserves, making it difficult to acquire enough dollars to convert all pesos. Panic selling of pesos could lead to chaos, and even maintaining a peso pegged to the dollar would require substantial forex reserves for defense. Despite Milei's ambitious ideas, he may find that conventional wisdom holds more value in the end, and the concern is that Argentinians may bear the cost of this realization.

### [Mamaearth’s IPO had lessons for investors](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/honasa-consumer-ltd-s-ipo-had-lessons-for-investors-11700578675084.html)

Honasa Consumer Ltd, the company behind the Mamaearth brand and other personal care products, recently listed on Indian stock exchanges through an initial public offering (IPO). The stock's issue price was ₹324, but it fell to a low of ₹256 on November 10th, recovering to close at around ₹367 on Tuesday.

The company's listing has raised concerns about allowing loss-making startups to sell shares to retail investors, particularly when a significant portion of its IPO is an 'offer for sale' that pays off existing investors. Furthermore, questions have been raised about whether equity mutual funds, which primarily invest retail money in stocks, should be allowed to invest in such stocks.

The IPO consisted of two parts: a majority was an offer for sale, which helped cash out existing shareholders, including promoters and investment firms. Additionally, Honasa Consumer raised ₹765.2 crore from anchor investors, including seven mutual funds and six insurance companies. This raises further questions as these funds mainly invest money raised from retail investors.

Notably, Honasa Consumer reported a loss of ₹151 crore in the last financial year, primarily due to exceptional items. The high valuation at which the stock was issued aligns with past IPOs of startups. When a large portion of an IPO is an offer for sale, retail investors' money indirectly helps facilitate an exit for existing investors at high valuations.

Although the amount invested by mutual funds in Honasa Consumer may seem small compared to their total investments, it raises concerns given past instances where mutual funds suffered losses from startup IPOs. It is essential to examine whether the mandate of mutual funds allows them to invest retail investors' money in such stocks.

The involvement of large cap schemes and various other schemes investing in Honasa Consumer also raises questions since the company does not rank among the top 100 stocks based on market capitalization. The Securities and Exchange Board of India should delve into this matter further, as it regulates the stock markets and mutual funds in the country.

Mutual funds have recently increased their stakes in startups after their stock prices had significantly fallen. This rush to invest in expensive IPOs may be influenced by the fact that mutual funds and insurance companies are often units of larger financial organizations running investment banks that manage IPOs.

Overall, there is a need for scrutiny and examination of these practices to ensure the protection of retail investors and prevent potential conflicts of interest.

The article concludes by emphasizing the importance of youth employment for India's demographic advantage and viewing the increase in female labor force participation as an opportunity rather than a distress-driven push. The latest Lancet Countdown report on climate change and health highlights the devastating impact of fossil fuel dependence on human health and the environment. The report reveals that the increasing frequency of heatwaves, droughts, and other extreme weather events has exposed millions of people to food insecurity and worsened air pollution, leading to a rise in infectious diseases. Despite the overwhelming evidence linking fossil fuel combustion to these health crises, world leaders have failed to take urgent action to phase out fossil fuels. If greenhouse gas emissions continue at the current rate, global temperatures could increase by nearly 3 degrees Celsius by 2100, resulting in catastrophic consequences for human health. The report calls for a comprehensive approach to address the climate crisis, including reducing emissions, transitioning to clean energy, implementing public health measures, and eliminating subsidies for fossil fuels. The health sector must play a leading role in this transition and advocate for policies that prioritize public health and well-being. The upcoming United Nations Climate Change Conference (CoP-28) is a crucial opportunity for world leaders to demonstrate their commitment to addressing the climate crisis and protecting human health.

Previous agreements with ASEAN, Japan, and South Korea have influenced India's trade dynamics and provided valuable experience for negotiating future agreements. Currently, India is preparing for a potentially significant FTA with the UK, which will set the template for future negotiations with the West and address non-trade issues such as environmental and labor standards. The negotiations will involve managing strategic trade-offs in various sectors, including dairy, wines and spirits, electrical and electronic items, and automotive tariffs and regulations. The EU's Carbon Border Adjustment Mechanism poses a challenge to India's exports of steel and aluminum to the EU. India has implemented measures such as the Production-Linked Incentive (PLI) scheme, trade facilitation initiatives, infrastructure development, and policy improvements to strengthen its trade integration efforts. However, challenges from new trade directions and the need for policy clarity, insight, and agility remain. India should conduct a comprehensive analysis of existing FTAs to inform future negotiations. Reforms to allow contract farming and create a national market for produce are also proposed. To finance and execute the SAP, a new institutional mechanism is needed for 5 to 7 years.

Considering India's federal structure, the article highlights the need for cooperation between the central and state governments in agricultural policy. ### [Less than four at one blow](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/columns/less-than-four-at-one-blow-11700159353369.html)

The article discusses W. Stanley Jevons' experiment on estimating the number of objects without counting them successively. Through his bean and box exercise conducted 1,027 times, Jevons found that he could accurately estimate the number when there were three or four beans, but made more mistakes with larger numbers. The article also mentions a recent study that found individual neurons in the brain responsible for perceiving specific numbers. Neurons tuned to small numbers were highly accurate, while those tuned to larger numbers were less precise. The study suggests that there is a boundary around the number four where our ability to estimate transitions from perceiving to estimating. This neurological mechanism involves the suppression of firing when offered the wrong number, improving accuracy. While the explanation is based on work with patients who have brain implants, it offers insight into how we estimate numbers. The author ends by wondering if they can train themselves to accurately guess larger sets of objects.

The article discusses the divergence between the Consumer Price Index (CPI) and Wholesale Price Index (WPI) in India and its impact on monetary policy. In 2015, India adopted an inflation targeting regime based on the CPI as recommended by the Urjit Patel Committee. The CPI was chosen over the WPI because it captured price movements in services and better represented consumers' inflation experience. The article highlights that inflation expectations closely followed the WPI until 2011, but the WPI started behaving differently after India's adoption of the inflation targeting regime. It notes that the WPI showed sustained periods of negative inflation, particularly in the manufacturing sector, which created disincentives for manufacturers. This divergence between the CPI and WPI poses a challenge for central banks, and some suggest that the producer price index (PPI) could be a better indicator for inflation targeting. The article concludes by proposing that the government should reconsider the legislative mandate and include both the WPI and CPI in the inflation target.

Wed, 15 Nov 2023 15:47:52 +0530
### [Mass bombardment should've been abandoned a long ago as a war strategy](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/mass-bombardment-shouldve-been-abandoned-a-long-ago-as-a-war-strategy-11700043053930.html)

During World War II, there were concerns about the psychological impact of bombings on British cities. However, studies conducted after the war showed that there was no evidence of a breakdown in morale among the affected population. In fact, bombings seemed to strengthen bonds between people and even stimulate the war-time economy in Germany. This counters the common belief that bombing a nation's infrastructure can break their will to fight. Human behavior adapts to dangerous situations, and people become numb to bombardment over time. Despite this knowledge, politicians often favor bombing strategies for their visible impact and ability to rally support during elections. The true impact of bombings is not straightforward and can have unintended consequences, such as cultivating hatred and extremism among victims. It is important to remember these lessons from history in conflicts like the one in Gaza.

### [Economic solutions aren’t helping us crack an air pollution problem](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/economic-solutions-aren-t-helping-us-crack-an-air-pollution-problem-11699970647360.html)

The article discusses the issue of pollution in Delhi and Mumbai, highlighting the factors contributing to the problem in both cities. In Mumbai, construction activities have significantly increased, leading to more construction dust and vehicular pollution. The decision to boost the construction sector by reducing premiums for real estate approvals has had first-order effects, but it has also resulted in higher-order effects such as poor air quality due to increased dust. 

Delhi, on the other hand, has been struggling with pollution for years despite having a well-developed metro network. While efforts have been made to curb pollution, such as shifting commercial transport to compressed natural gas and improving emission standards for vehicles, rice stubble burning by farmers in Punjab and Haryana remains a major contributor to pollution. This practice is an example of the tragedy of the commons, where individual actions collectively create a significant problem.

To address these issues, coercion or incentives are suggested to discourage stubble burning and encourage farmers to grow crops other than rice. Similarly, policies limiting car usage or promoting public transportation face resistance from car owners. The article raises the question of why planners didn't anticipate the need for longer platforms in the Delhi Metro to accommodate more people during peak hours.

Overall, the article emphasizes that pollution is a complex problem with no simple solutions. It requires collective efforts and interventions from governments and individuals to address the various contributing factors effectively.

### [The US-China decoupling is slow going but still offers India opportunities](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-us-china-decoupling-is-slow-going-but-still-offers-india-opportunities-11699956240679.html)

The United States is reducing its dependence on Chinese imports to the lowest level in 17 years, with Mexico and Canada surpassing China as the top exporters to the US. However, the situation is more complex than it appears. China may adjust its strategy to bypass US actions by finding new channels to export goods. A study by World Bank economists reveals that higher US tariffs on Chinese imports have affected China's market share in targeted goods, but overall US imports have not decreased. This suggests that the US is sourcing these products from other countries instead of manufacturing them domestically. The trade war with China has led to increased imports from other developing countries like Vietnam or Mexico, resulting in higher prices for US consumers. The study also highlights that one dominant beneficiary captures the benefits of each trade line, signaling a "China plus one" strategy. Additionally, many countries reporting increased exports to the US are also reporting a corresponding increase in imports from China, indicating that the US is still connected to Chinese supply chains through its new dominant trade partners. The ultimate outcome of this trade tussle is uncertain, but it is clear that the decoupling of the two largest economies will not be painless. Financial flows and trade imbalances also complicate the situation. Rewiring global supply chains due to the US-China conflict is leading to a new form of globalization rather than full-scale deglobalization. India stands to benefit from this reshuffling of trade partners, given its growing internal market and position as a counterweight to China. However, India needs a more open trade policy and the ability to participate in major trading blocs for further gains.

### [The SC’s ruling on personal debt guarantees will help unlock dead capital](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-sc-s-ruling-on-personal-debt-guarantees-will-help-unlock-dead-capital-11699884806982.html)

The adoption of the Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code (IBC) in 2016 was a significant economic reform that aimed to resolve bankruptcies and transfer assets to new owners in a systematic and time-bound manner. The IBC introduced a time limit for debt restructuring or resolution, and if a satisfactory resolution couldn't be reached within that timeframe, the asset would automatically go into liquidation. The law has undergone amendments to address loopholes and prevent owners of failed enterprises from re-acquiring distressed assets during the liquidation process. However, there have been challenges, such as cases exceeding the time limit and a relatively low realization ratio for creditors. The IBC's impact on credit discipline and the recent Supreme Court decision upholding its provisions related to personal guarantors are positive developments. Overall, the IBC is continuously being strengthened to unlock unproductive or dead capital.

### [From climate pledges to action: unbiased data is a must for strong regulation](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/from-climate-pledges-to-action-unbiased-data-is-a-must-for-strong-regulation-11699859627577.html)

Hmm, I am not sure. Email support@chatbase.co for more info.Hmm, I am not sure. Email support@chatbase.co for more info.The Paris climate agreement, established in 2015, has encouraged countries to commit to reducing greenhouse gas emissions. However, a recent report by the United Nations indicates that we are not making sufficient progress in achieving the necessary cuts to combat climate change. This highlights the urgent need for governments to take swift and decisive action to keep global warming within safe limits.

Four key economic sectors, namely industry, transportation, electricity, and buildings, account for 75% of global emissions. Implementing well-designed public policies in these sectors can effectively reduce pollution, promote consumer savings, protect public health, and stimulate sustainable economic growth.

Transforming our fossil-fuel-based economies in time to avoid climate catastrophe and meet energy needs is a daunting task. It requires technical, economic, and political expertise, along with significant financial resources and labor. However, the agencies responsible for devising and implementing these crucial policies often lack adequate staffing and funding. Additionally, they may have to rely on information provided by the industries they regulate, leading to weak regulations and missed objectives.

To address this power imbalance, independent non-governmental organizations (NGOs) play a crucial role by providing policymakers with the information and technical knowledge needed to design robust regulations that effectively reduce harmful emissions. For example, the US Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) received contradictory data from industry bodies when drafting rules to limit greenhouse gas emissions from heavy-duty vehicles. An independent think tank called the International Council on Clean Transportation (ICCT) conducted its own comprehensive study and provided the EPA with impartial analysis and cost projections, resulting in stringent regulations that are expected to lead to significant emission cuts, fuel cost savings, and environmental damage prevention.

NGOs like the ICCT can also assist emerging economies with limited resources in initiating transformative climate programs. By facilitating the adoption of clean-energy solutions, these organizations can increase access to affordable and pollution-free electricity. Furthermore, promoting the use of innovative technologies through regulations can drive innovation, enhance competitiveness, and position countries as climate leaders.

An example of this is India's nationwide appliance-efficiency program launched in 2006. Collaborating with NGOs such as CLASP and The Energy and Resources Institute (TERI), Indian officials were able to adapt successful efficiency-labeling programs to their market. These partnerships resulted in the rapid implementation of efficiency programs and substantial GHG emissions reductions. India has also become a leading manufacturer of energy-efficient air conditioners.

Unbiased research provided by independent NGOs equips regulators with the data necessary to develop transparent and effective environmental policies. As developing and developed economies strengthen their capacities, they will gain more confidence in setting ambitious targets, creating a positive cycle. With appropriate support, we can ensure that future generations are proud of the progress made in addressing the climate crisis.

### [Rise in infant mortality shows that the US needs to take better care of its moms](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/rise-in-infant-mortality-shows-that-the-us-needs-to-take-better-care-of-its-moms-11699859722434.html)

According to new provisional data from the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), the infant death rate in the US increased by 3% in 2022 to 5.6 deaths per 1,000 live births. This is the first significant increase in about 20 years. It is too early to determine if this is the start of a troubling trend or just one bad year, as more data and time will be needed to understand the factors behind the rise in infant deaths.

The data reveals important truths about the state of infant and maternal health care in the US, which could potentially worsen. Even a single year's increase in infant deaths, especially when the rate already surpasses that of other economically similar countries, should be seen as a sign that more effort is needed to address the issue.

The increase in infant deaths was most notable among babies born to Alaska Native, American Indian, and Caucasian women, as well as premature and early preterm births. Additionally, more deaths were attributed to maternal complications and bacterial sepsis.

Public health experts emphasize that without further information, it is premature to conclude why more babies died last year. However, they highlight the importance of considering maternal health alongside infant deaths, as failures in one area reflect failures in the other. Pressures on reproductive health, such as limited access to abortion care services, rising maternal mortality rates, inadequate maternal care in certain areas, and lack of insurance coverage, contribute to the overall challenges faced in improving maternal and infant health.

Maternal deaths in the US have more than doubled between 1999 and 2019, with American Indian, Alaska Native, and African-American women experiencing higher rates. Although provisional CDC data indicate some improvement in 2022 and 2023, the rates remain significantly higher than before the COVID-19 pandemic. Policy changes, such as extending Medicaid coverage for postpartum women, have been implemented in several states, but the removal of Medicaid coverage for millions of people during the pandemic raises concerns about the potential worsening of infant and maternal mortality rates due to inadequate care.

While it might be tempting to connect newly implemented abortion bans to the increase in infant deaths, it is too early to determine if there is a broader correlation. States with abortion restrictions already had higher infant and maternal mortality rates, and these restrictions could lead to a higher proportion of areas lacking obstetric providers and hospitals offering maternity care.

Researchers will continue to analyze the events of 2022 to understand how to prevent further infant mortality in the US. However, there are already significant factors undermining maternal and infant health in the country. The question remains whether policies to improve obstetric care can keep pace with policies that undermine it.

### [The comet exploded, or it didn’t](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/columns/the-comet-exploded-or-it-didnt-11699552634327.html)

Hmm, I am not sure. Email support@chatbase.co for more info.Hmm, I am not sure. Email support@chatbase.co for more info.In February 2022, a team of scientists led by geologist Kenneth Tankersley published a paper in Nature magazine, presenting their findings on the so-called Hopewell people who lived in the Ohio River valley over 1,500 years ago. Their remarkable claim was that a comet explosion, or a "cosmic airburst event," occurred in the valley during the 3rd or 4th Century CE, which contributed to the cultural decline of the Hopewell people.

The team provided several pieces of evidence to support their theory, including the construction of a "comet-shaped earthwork" near the epicenter, the presence of meteorites and surfaces exposed to extreme heat, and the discovery of microspherules, which are known to be produced by meteors entering Earth's atmosphere.

However, just months later, German astronomers Ralph and Dagmar Neuhäuser published a paper challenging Tankersley's findings. They argued that the evidence presented did not support the idea of a comet or its explosion. They disputed Tankersley's claim of an increased risk of such events during that time period, pointing out that the historical record Tankersley referenced was for a different timeframe. They also questioned the assumption that the earthwork was comet-related and the idea that the Hopewell people would build such a structure after a catastrophic event.

Tankersley and his team responded to the Neuhäusers' critique, refuting some of their points and emphasizing the inherent ambiguity in explaining ancient airburst events and tracing the origin of impactors on Earth.

A year later, another group of researchers published a critical rebuttal of the airburst hypothesis and evidence, further undermining Tankersley's theory. They argued that the chronological analysis did not support the notion of a single event, that the burned surfaces were used for ceremonial fires, and that the microspherules were found away from other evidence of the airburst and likely of local origin. They accused Tankersley's team of misrepresenting primary sources, using flawed analyses, and inaccurately characterizing the source of supposed extraterrestrial materials.

Ultimately, Tankersley's paper was retracted by Nature, as the editors no longer had confidence in its conclusions. Tankersley and his team did not respond to correspondence regarding the retraction.

Despite the failure of Tankersley's theory, this episode highlights the progress of science. It shows how mistakes are called out and how scientific ideas are challenged and refined through critical examination and evidence-based arguments. In this case, the scientific establishment reacted appropriately by retracting the article and acknowledging the lack of support for the conclusions presented.

### [The Old Pension Scheme is fiscally risky but there's a case for it too](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-old-pension-scheme-is-fiscally-risky-but-theres-a-case-for-it-too-11699524898693.html)

The Old Pension Scheme (OPS) is seen as detrimental to public finances because it involves paying retired personnel a pension from government revenue for their entire lives. The OPS guarantees a pension amounting to 50% of the last pay drawn. In contrast, the New Pension Scheme (NPS), which is currently in place, requires employees to contribute from their salary, with the government matching the contribution. The NPS provides payouts from a pension fund upon retirement but does not burden the government with liability. Some states are considering returning to the OPS, despite criticism of its populist nature.

The ability of budgets to support pension expenditure is a crucial concern. As per Reserve Bank of India data, pensions account for around 40% of the salary bill in all states. This burden will continue to increase due to more retirees and periodic adjustments for inflation. This rising payout burden may lead to less funding for capital expenditure and other development efforts.

However, from a Rawlsian perspective of justice in public finance, reviving the OPS can be seen as fair since switching to the NPS discriminates between old and new government employees. It is argued that employees doing the same work in the same organization should not be treated differently based on an arbitrary cut-off date.

Private sector compensation packages follow a cost-to-company (CTC) approach, where benefits are incorporated into the pay package. Implementing a similar CTC policy in the government sector would inflate the salary bill and draw criticism. The concept of deferred payments through pensions was aimed at offering old-age social security while controlling immediate government expenses.

The broader issue lies in the role of the state in the economy, with a shift towards making government revenue work better. Traditionally focused on redistribution and providing public services, governments now face pressure to align spending with private interests. Salaries and pensions are considered "committed expenditure," and there is a need to balance compensations and rationalize structures.

One proposed solution is to raise the salaries of those under the NPS to achieve parity and rework perquisites within government departments. Pensions have a positive multiplier effect on the economy as retirees tend to spend their pensions, contributing to demand across all age groups. The author suggests that India's Pay Commission should consider these proposals and make recommendations accordingly.

Please note that these are the personal views of the author.

### [A thin line separates economic nationalism from a closed economy but it can work](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/a-thin-line-separates-economic-nationalism-from-a-closed-economy-but-it-can-work-11699444784146.html)

The article discusses the rise of economic nationalism and its implications for global trade. While some view economic nationalism as a return to protectionism and autarky, it can be both harmful and beneficial depending on its form. Economic nationalism, like political nationalism, prioritizes the nation's interests in framing the economy. However, its definition varies and could involve measures that either restrict or leverage international links to promote national economic growth.

Countries in East Asia, such as Japan, South Korea, Taiwan, and China, have successfully combined economic nationalism with policies that encourage global economic integration and protect key industries. These countries utilized industrial policies, subsidies, and trade barriers strategically to develop their economic competence and catch up with the West. Despite accusations of insufficient market access, East Asia's economic nationalism has benefited the rest of the world by creating larger markets and lowering prices for consumers.

However, economic nationalism can also go wrong when governments engage in excessive state control, support inefficient firms for too long, or close their economies indiscriminately. In such cases, the negative consequences primarily affect the country itself rather than its neighbors. The article suggests that if the US focuses on creating a strong domestic economy through economic nationalism, it can revive the tradition of developmentalism and benefit other countries as well. The risk lies in the US overstepping its boundaries and imposing its preferences on others, which would harm the world and provide little benefit to itself.

### [The Old Pension Scheme wildfire must be stopped before it’s too late](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-old-pension-scheme-wildfire-must-be-stopped-before-it-s-too-late-11699371711297.html)

The political battle between the National Pension System (NPS) and the Old Pension Scheme (OPS) is intensifying due to ongoing state elections in India. The Congress party's victory in the Himachal Pradesh elections is being attributed to their promise of bringing back OPS. However, attributing the victory solely to this issue may be misleading. The NPS was introduced in 2004 by the National Democratic Alliance government, and it is argued that electoral outcomes are influenced more by emotional issues rather than pension systems. Public opinion is being swayed by presenting OPS as 'pro-people' and NPS as 'anti-people'. While the NPS can be adjusted to address concerns, resurrecting OPS would be a setback for fiscal stability. OPS represents mounting unfunded obligations for governments, leading to potential bankruptcy. On the other hand, NPS involves joint contributions from employees and employers, eliminating unfunded obligations post-retirement. Several states have expressed an intention to join the OPS bandwagon, but calculations show that this would lead to a significant burden on state finances. The expenditure on pensions as a share of states' own revenues has increased from 7.9% in 1990-91 to 27.4% in 2020-21. Despite covering only 3.2% of India's workforce, pensions consume 18% of government revenues. In contrast, developed countries have transitioned to pension systems with defined contributions and smaller expenditure shares. India's fiscal situation is concerning, with high debt-to-GDP ratios and rapid aging expected in the future. These centers aim to develop scalable AI solutions in areas like agriculture, health, and sustainable cities. AI is being leveraged in India to create grassroots impact. For example, the AI Sowing App provides farmers in Karnataka and Andhra Pradesh with advisories on optimal sowing dates, depths, and fertilizer application schedules. This app has helped farmers boost crop yields by 10%-30% without requiring advanced equipment. This demonstrates how AI can be a force multiplier in addressing pressing challenges faced by society and industry.

It can streamline administrative procedures, improve decision-making, provide personalized care, and aid in early disease detection. This leads to increased accuracy, decreased defects, and reduced waste. As India aims to incentivize manufacturing within the country, AI presents an opportunity to leapfrog with IoT and smart manufacturing systems.

In the knowledge economy, AI-assisted tools like GitHub Copilot are helping software developers increase productivity. By focusing on the big picture, developers can come up with innovative solutions while AI assists with complex tasks and routine coding processes.

Investing in AI education and training programs can empower India's youth, reduce income gaps, and bridge the digital divide. Cloud and AI-powered education platforms can scale skill-building initiatives, personalize learning, and improve educational outcomes.

The future with AI is one where people are empowered to be their creative best, with AI acting as a companion to assist with routine and complex tasks. India has a unique opportunity to unlock the creative potential of its young workforce and lead with AI.

### [China may have to slow down in the superpower race and tackle domestic problems](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/china-may-have-to-slow-down-in-the-superpower-race-and-tackle-domestic-problems-11699270673674.html)

China's medium-term economic prospects are deteriorating rapidly. The country's economy grew at an average annual rate of 9% from 2000 to 2019, but since then, it has grown at half that rate and in a volatile pattern. China is currently grappling with deflationary slowdown, reflected in the latest Consumer Price Inflation number of -0.3%. The prospects of exceeding 5% growth over the medium-term are diminishing due to cyclical and structural reasons.

In 2019, when the Chinese economy was performing well, the government implemented measures to increase the state's role and suppress market forces. However, this shift towards a state-directed model now appears to have been a hasty mistake. China's anti-espionage law has also made it difficult for foreign businesses to operate in the country, resulting in declining foreign direct investment.

The COVID-19 pandemic and China's strict lockdown measures have had a negative impact on its economy. The property market is experiencing plunging prices, over-leveraged companies, unsold inventory, and suppressed demand. Evergrande, a major property company, is facing a debt load of over $300 billion and has defaulted on some of its foreign debt. This situation is representative of the entire debt-ridden sector.

China's efforts to diversify its economy towards domestic consumption have failed to gain traction. Consumer sentiment remains below pre-pandemic levels, and excessive household savings have not translated into increased consumption due to depressed real estate values.

Furthermore, China is facing a demographic decline as a result of its one-child policy. Youth unemployment is high, suggesting that growth estimates may be exaggerated. There is also a crisis of confidence among private businesses and consumers.

While it may be premature to declare a permanent slowdown in China, the country may need to rely on monetary and fiscal policy measures to counteract the economic challenges it faces. However, with a substantial public debt burden, China is hesitant to dramatically ease policy. It may also need to curb its spending on geo-strategic projects in order to address its economic issues.

China's rivalry with the US as a global superpower is ongoing, but China is falling further behind its rival. This may cause China to be more cautious or more belligerent in its actions. The hope is that China chooses the former for the sake of peace and stability.

### [Goldin’s Nobel win has placed Women’s economics’ at the heart of the discipline](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/goldins-nobel-win-has-placed-women-s-economics-at-the-heart-of-the-discipline-11699269628776.html)

Harvard economist Claudia Goldin has won the Nobel Prize in Economics for her research on women's labor-market outcomes. Her work focuses on gender issues that are often marginalized in the field of economics, such as women's labor-force participation and the gender pay gap. Goldin's research challenges traditional theories of economic development by showing that female labor-force participation follows a U-shaped curve over time, with women joining the workforce at higher rates once the services sector gains dominance. She also demonstrates that the gender pay gap is primarily due to childbirth-related factors, such as career interruptions and reductions in working hours. Additionally, Goldin highlights the importance of women's expectations and societal changes in shaping their professional prospects. Her scholarship emphasizes the need for economics to consider historical context, disaggregate economic agents, and address intimate aspects of life, such as marriage and child-rearing. From a policy perspective, Goldin suggests re-imagining either marriage and child-rearing or the economy itself to better support women's economic success. If no action is taken, women will continue to face challenges in balancing domestic responsibilities with income and independence.

### [Stricter capital rules for US banks are a lazy way to keep them safe](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/stricter-capital-rules-for-us-banks-are-a-lazy-way-to-keep-them-safe-11698993431051.html)

US regulators are considering imposing higher capital requirements on banks with over $100 billion in assets in response to the banking failures of March 2023. However, some argue that this is a puzzling choice as smaller banks have been found to engage in more egregious risk-taking. While some proposed changes, such as including unrealized gains and losses from certain securities in capital ratios, are overdue, CEOs of large banks are not pleased with the stricter rules. They argue that it could stymie economic growth by prompting lenders to pull back. The article explores the role of bank capital in providing stability to the banking system and the economy. It highlights that more capital means fewer runs by uninsured depositors and a more stable banking system. However, it also acknowledges that the issue is more complicated than that. The article discusses how higher capital requirements can reduce run-prone borrowing and provide a loss-absorbing buffer for banks. It also explains how capital regulation allows profitable banks to grow while restraining loss-making banks. Additionally, it notes that a minimum capital requirement acts as an entry ticket for banks to raise capital at a reasonable cost and serves as a gauge of a bank's performance for the public. The article questions whether raising capital requirements is appropriate today and argues against the rationale that it gives bank boards and equity holders more incentive to limit risk-taking. It suggests that board members are dependent on management and may not restrain risky behavior. Furthermore, it argues that capital regulation may fail to limit a bank's pursuit of tail risks that earn profits until bad times come. The article also discusses the potential offsetting cost of higher capital requirements, as more capital gives bank management a longer leash to take excessive risks before facing consequences. It suggests that occasional depositor runs can have a salutary effect if they incentivize prudent management. However, it warns against making banks so thinly capitalized that small losses can precipitate panics and larger losses. It acknowledges that higher capital requirements can make capital costlier and potentially inhibit banks' ability to finance growth. It also raises concerns about activity migrating to institutions with lower capital requirements, which could make the system less safe. The article concludes by emphasizing the importance of sensible regulation and knowing when a tool loses its effectiveness and becomes counterproductive.

### [Promotions, salary hikes and training are necessary to retain good employees](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/promotions-salary-hikes-and-training-are-necessary-to-retain-good-employees-11698907747536.html)

A recent study by the ADP Research Institute found that 29% of employees quit their employer within a month after receiving their first promotion, compared to only 18% of non-promoted workers. This gap persisted for about six months and was particularly pronounced for managers. The study suggests that getting a promotion increases a person's perceived value, making them more attractive to recruiters. However, the article argues that the high turnover rate may be due to frustrating promotion practices at many companies. Some organizations only offer promotions when an employee has a written offer from a rival, which does not inspire loyalty. Additionally, many new managers do not receive leadership training until they have been in the role for years, leading to feelings of being left to sink or swim on their own. Lack of training is compounded by lack of time, as mid-level managers are expected to both do the work and supervise it. Money is also a factor, as it can be harder to get a significant raise with an internal promotion compared to switching companies. Many HR departments have rules limiting the percentage increase an employee can receive with a promotion, which can make loyal employees feel undervalued. External hires often receive higher pay than newly promoted internal candidates, even though they initially perform worse. While changing jobs can bring short-term financial gains, it may slow down future raises and promotions. Lower-paid workers have the most to gain from changing jobs, according to analysts at Bank of America. The article concludes by advising employers to take promotions seriously and provide training and support to promote success in new roles, along with salaries that reflect the increased responsibilities.

### [An India-UK investment treaty might soon be clinched](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/an-india-uk-investment-treaty-might-soon-be-clinched-11698851458322.html)

India and the UK are moving closer to signing a Free Trade Agreement (FTA), with negotiations currently at an advanced stage. Contentious issues such as intellectual property rights, rules of origin, and a bilateral investment treaty (BIT) have been under discussion. The two countries have made progress on dispute settlement, which was a major point of disagreement in the BIT. India terminated all its 83 BITs with foreign countries in 2016, including the one with the UK, following a case involving Australia. The UK was not keen on including an exhaustion of local remedies (ELR) clause in the dispute settlement provisions, but India insisted on it. The ELR clause requires investors to exhaust domestic remedies before initiating international arbitration. India's unease with investors going directly for international arbitration is understandable given its experience as a respondent in investment treaty arbitrations. However, both sides have shown flexibility in negotiations, and India may drop its insistence on the ELR clause. Another issue is India's narrowed-down definition of 'investment' for BIT protection, which has shifted from an 'asset' based to an 'enterprise' based definition. The asset-based definition covers all kinds of assets that cross borders, while the enterprise-based approach narrows the scope of protected investments. Indian policymakers have indicated that concessions may need to be made on the model BIT for trade partners like the UK. If a mutually acceptable BIT is signed between India and the UK, it would be a significant achievement for India as it has not signed any BIT with a major economy since adopting its model BIT.

### [India’s new investors can learn a few old lessons from Mr Chicken](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-new-investors-can-learn-a-few-old-lessons-from-mr-chicken-11698766076146.html)

The hashtag #stockmarketcrash trended on social media platform X (formerly Twitter) when the S&P BSE SmallCap Index fell around 2-2.3% from its previous close. However, this drop was not significant in the broader context of the stock market. The rise in individual investors in recent years has led to increased investment in small cap stocks, driving up their valuations. ### [Don’t let meaningless phrases get in the way of climate action](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/dont-let-meaningless-phrases-get-in-the-way-of-climate-action-11698753258519.html)

The term "unabated" is being used in discussions about phasing out fossil fuels, but its meaning is often unclear. The European Union and businesses worth almost $1 trillion are calling for the discontinuation of unabated hydrocarbons. US climate envoy John Kerry wants to end new unabated coal-fired power plants. However, the lack of a clear definition for unabated leaves room for continued fossil fuel production under the promise of future abatement. Abatement regulations should cover the entire emissions life cycle and include carbon capture and storage (CCS) and methane leakage reduction. Strong abatement regulations have had a significant impact in the UK, where no new coal plants have been built. However, CCS capacity is currently insufficient to meet net-zero emissions targets by 2050. Additionally, carbon capture does not address other harmful emissions from fossil fuels. As countries negotiate at CoP-28, it is important to establish clear abatement standards to ensure meaningful action on phasing out unabated fossil fuels.

These stores, which blend traditional and modern retail elements, offer consumers a diverse product range and a modern shopping experience locally. They also benefit brands by providing valuable customer data. With over 25,000 outlets, predominantly in smaller towns, these stores are giving stiff competition to large retailers and are expected to continue co-existing with other retail formats. This evolution in the retail sector is driven by factors such as increased income and consumption expenditure, improved supply chains, digital adoption, and changing social dynamics.

Tue, 31 Oct 2023 10:00:15 +0530
### [Peaches, coffee and now olive oil: Climate change can alter our food basket](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/peaches-coffee-and-now-olive-oil-climate-change-can-alter-our-food-basket-11698672313859.html)

The global output of olive oil this year is expected to be significantly lower than the five-year average due to drought, floods, and forest fires in olive-growing regions, all of which are attributed to global warming. Climate change affects agriculture by causing extreme and unpredictable weather events that damage crops and changing climatic conditions that make certain crops unsuitable for their traditional growing geographies. Coffee production is also impacted, with the Arabica variety expected to decrease while the Robusta variety gains ground. Climate change raises the average temperature of the earth's surface, leading to changes in sub-tropical regions and potential melting of glaciers and permafrost. Adapting to climate change poses political challenges for countries like India, as it requires identifying new crops, training farmers, establishing new supply chains, and potentially switching from water-intensive crops like sugarcane. Building climate resilience in agriculture requires technological agility, policy adaptation, flexible public finance, and investments in irrigation and drainage capacity. Ensuring food security also involves maintaining infrastructure, protecting coastal towns from erosion and storms, and preparing people for evacuation.

The broader economy is also at risk, as India's tech professionals have been a key driver of the nation's middle class and overall growth.

### [It often takes more resolve and grit to save lives than wage war](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/it-often-takes-more-resolve-and-grit-to-save-lives-than-wage-war-11698677910214.html)

This article discusses a pivotal moment during the Cold War in 1962 when the US and Soviet Union were on the brink of nuclear war. The Kennedy administration discovered that the Soviets had positioned nuclear missiles in Cuba, leading to a total blockade of Cuba by the US. Four Soviet submarines carrying nuclear-tipped torpedoes were ordered to sail towards the blockade. The US Navy dropped depth charges to force the submarines to surface, but the submarines had lost contact with Moscow and were uncertain if war had already begun. Captain Valentin Savitsky decided to launch a nuclear torpedo, but Vasily Arkhipov, the executive officer, disagreed and convinced the captain to surface and try contacting Moscow. The submarine eventually established communication with its headquarters and returned. This incident is considered one of the most dangerous moments in history, and it highlights the importance of cool-headed decision-making in times of war. The article also draws parallels between this historical event and current conflicts, such as Israel's ground invasion of Gaza and tensions with Iran. It emphasizes the irony of how warriors who wage war are often celebrated, while those who strive to prevent war are overlooked.

However, investors should be cautious of crypto schemes that may appear strong but prove unstable in practice.

### [Flipkart losses show difficulty of catering to discount-crazy Indians](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/flipkart-losses-show-difficulty-of-catering-to-discount-crazy-indians-11698228544754.html)

India's e-commerce players, Flipkart and Amazon, have experienced a record festival season with a combined 186 million customer visits in the first 48 hours of their sales. Flipkart expects a gross merchandise value (GMV) of ₹36,000 crore, while Redseer Strategy Consultants projected a GMV of over ₹90,000 crore for the month-long spree. Redseer had forecasted that this year's festive season shopping spree would be the biggest on record, with shoppers expected to spend 20% more than last year. Wide-spectrum platforms like Flipkart and Amazon face challenges from niche retailers and policy roadblocks. Additionally, they face competition from Reliance Retail and the Tata Group, as well as pushback from offline retail. The surge in volumes is supported by investments in logistics infrastructure but relies on deep discounts to drive sales. Weaning Indian e-shoppers off their discount habit will be crucial for these platforms to achieve profitability.

### [Either repeal or revise the country’s fiscal law](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/either-repeal-or-revise-the-country-s-fiscal-law-11698159666202.html)

The article discusses India's fiscal position and the need to reconsider the Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management (FRBM) Act. Despite the act's 3% deficit cap being almost twice the limit specified by fiscal law, it has been largely ignored and considered outdated. The article argues that fiscal policy should not be constrained by rigid laws and that state spending plays a vital role in stimulating the economy during trying times. The recent experience of large deficits during the pandemic has not led to inflation or high lending rates, suggesting that the FRBM Act's restrictions may have been misjudged. However, given the risks of overspending, it is suggested that the government should tighten its fiscal position faster than required by its stated glide path.

### [India’s DPI approach could yet rival the Brussels Effect](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indias-dpi-approach-could-yet-rival-the-brussels-effect-11698159619058.html)

The European Union's General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) has had a significant global impact, with over 150 countries incorporating its principles into their own laws. This influence is known as the Brussels Effect. The EU's large single market and cleverly designed regulations that apply to activities outside its borders contribute to its regulatory dominance. Europe's impressive regulatory infrastructure, including powerful institutions and a commitment to economic union, further strengthens its position. In contrast, China lacks a similar infrastructure, and the US lacks the political will to consistently enforce regulations. However, concerns have been raised about the inconvenience and high costs of GDPR compliance. India has proposed a new approach to data governance called Digital Public Infrastructure (DPI), which embeds regulatory principles into digital infrastructure code. Strong regulatory institutions and a commitment to techno-legal governance are necessary for this approach to be successful globally.

Tue, 24 Oct 2023 21:41:34 +0530
### [The fast growth in non-housing personal loans ought to worry us](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/the-fast-growth-in-non-housing-personal-loans-ought-to-worry-us-11698159554347.html)

Shaktikanta Das, the governor of the Reserve Bank of India (RBI), has expressed concerns about the rapid growth of certain components of personal loans. The term "personal loans" refers to retail loans, including housing loans, credit card outstandings, vehicle loans, education loans, and more. As of August 2023, outstanding personal loans have increased by 30.8% compared to August 2022. However, this figure does not account for the merger between home-loan lender HDFC and HDFC Bank in July. When considering data from June-end, outstanding personal loans grew by 20.9%. Das's statement likely refers to the non-housing part of personal loans, which grew by 26.7% in June and have been growing at a rate greater than 20% since June 2022. The share of these loans in personal loans reached a high of 53.1% in June. This growth in personal loans is concerning because most of these loans are used for immediate consumption or purchasing depreciating assets. Banks are now more inclined to give out personal loans rather than lending to industry due to various factors such as the aftermath of previous borrowing binge and easier recovery from individual defaulters. There could be several reasons for this jump in personal loans, including revenge consumption after the pandemic and financing expenses through loans, struggling income levels leading to borrowing, and a K-shaped economic recovery where the rich and well-to-do take on a greater proportion of these loans. Interestingly, the rapid growth in non-housing personal loans has occurred despite rising interest rates. This suggests that individuals taking on these loans are not bothered by higher monthly installments, indicating a K-shaped economic recovery and struggles on the income front.

### [Indian urban planning needs a major overhaul](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/indian-urban-planning-needs-a-major-overhaul-11698071809104.html)

A survey conducted by think-tank Janaagraha has highlighted the shortcomings of urban planning in India. The survey found that low levels of governance and fiscal autonomy, along with inadequate information and weak public accountability, are hindering the development of urban spaces in the country. By 2050, it is estimated that over 800 million people will be living in Indian cities, necessitating robust municipal bodies to handle the increased civic burden. However, most cities in India are poorly run and lack the necessary reforms to empower local authorities. The survey also revealed that many cities lack active plans for spatial development and key urban needs. The problem is more pronounced in smaller cities. The politicization of big city municipalities has made them unresponsive to the concerns of urban residents. Mumbai, for example, has slums without basic civic services alongside upmarket suburbs. The lack of human resources dedicated to municipal tasks exacerbates the situation, with Indian cities having far fewer staff compared to international counterparts like New York and London. Additionally, weak devolution of administrative authority and limited access to financial resources further hinder urban development. To address these issues, urban reforms should focus on meaningful public representation, greater fiscal autonomy for municipal bodies, and exploring alternative revenue sources such as road pricing. It is crucial for Indian cities to improve their infrastructure and services to be recognized as world-class destinations and successfully host major events like the Olympics.

### [The internet cheapened news but AI could reverse that trend](https://www.livemint.com/opinion/online-views/the-internet-cheapened-news-but-ai-could-reverse-that-trend-11698064813683.html)

The problem of misinformation online continues to persist, and tech companies may never be able to fully eradicate it. However, trusted sources of information can play a crucial role in combating fake news. In the context of the Israel-Gaza conflict, misinformation takes various forms, such as old videos being re-captioned to appear new and relevant. The volume of misinformation on platforms like Twitter is overwhelming, and efforts to debunk false footage often fall short. The use of artificial intelligence (AI) is set to supercharge the spread of misinformation, making it even more challenging to address. Technological solutions like fact-checking processes are often slow and ineffective. Furthermore, the trust in tech companies has been undermined by recent events, such as Elon Musk's actions and Meta Platforms' shift away from caring about news content. The rise of AI-generated deepfakes further complicates the issue, as tools to detect them are flawed and will become less effective over time. This "Age of Unreality" erodes trust in what we see and hear. Despite these challenges, news websites remain a reliable source of trusted information. Direct traffic to news websites has been increasing since the pandemic began, suggesting that readers find comfort and clarity in established news organizations. However, news organizations must invest more time in explaining their work and earning readers' trust. Open Source Intelligence operations like Bellingcat serve as a model for transparent news gathering. AI poses a significant disruption to the news industry but also highlights the value of honest journalism.

High-impact journals often prioritize newsworthy papers, allowing scientists to exaggerate the significance of their work. While there are concerns about Dias's research integrity, some physicists believe his findings might still be accurate, albeit achieved through data manipulation. Superconductors, which are materials that allow electricity to flow without resistance, have been a sought-after phenomenon, particularly at higher temperatures. However, even if Dias's claims are true, a room-temperature superconductor may still require cooling for practical applications. Retractions in scientific journals are not uncommon, with suspected data manipulation and misconduct being the primary reasons. The culture of celebrity in scientific research can lead to exaggeration and a failure to critically evaluate research integrity.
